Obstacles to Accepting the Prophet's Call
Nasafi lists four obstacles that prevent people from responding to the Prophet's call.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four main obstacles that prevent people from accepting the Prophet's message, as identified by Nasafi.

Core Idea
Even when truth is clear, people reject it due to bias, pride, attachment, or laziness.

After establishing the Prophet's truthfulness, Nasafi turns to why people still reject the message. He identifies four psychological and social barriers that hinder acceptance, showing that rejection is often not due to intellectual deficiency but to personal inclinations.

Guided Path
1

The obstacles are labeled a, b, c, d.
2

Find the four obstacles: racial partisanship, pride, familiarity/desire, and laziness. Understand the meaning of each.
These are psychological and social, not intellectual.
3
Reflect on contemporary relevance
Think about how these same obstacles exist today. Why might people reject truth even when it is clearly presented?
Consider examples from your own experience.

Nasafi's Classification of the Properties of Prophethood
Nasafi divides the special characteristics of prophethood into two main categories, each with two subdivisions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi categorizes the special characteristics of prophethood into two main divisions and their subdivisions, and why each element is significant.

Core Idea
Prophethood's properties are perfectly balanced: foundation and nurture, each with two essential features.

Imam Nasafi, in his Tabsirat al-Adilla, provides a concise yet profound classification of the distinctive traits (khaṣāʾiṣ) of prophethood. He organizes them into two main categories: those that establish the foundation and those that nurture the prophetic powers. Each category is further subdivided, giving us a clear framework to appreciate the completeness of the Prophet Muhammad's prophethood. This passage presents that elegant structure.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the overall structure. Notice the two main divisions.
2
Examine the first division and its subdivisions
Identify the two elements under the first division: genetic choice (noble lineage) and perfection of virtues. Reflect on why each is essential for prophethood.
3
Examine the second division and its subdivisions
Identify the two elements under the second division: continuous revelation and divine correction. Consider how these show divine care.
4
Synthesize the complete picture
Notice that the passage concludes that all these properties were fully realized in Prophet Muhammad. Reflect on how this classification defends the integrity of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد ذلك يتحدث عن خواص النبوة ويجملها في قسمين الأول: لتمهيد أمرها وتوطيد أساسها. والثاني – لتربية قواها . ويقسم الأول إلى قسمين أحدهما - الاختيار الجنسي، ويتوفر فيه الشرف. والثاني - توفر القوى الفاضلة فيه، وإبعاد العلل عنه، فلقد كان كامل العقل، والخلق، والخلقة. أما القسم الثاني فيقسمه إلى قسمين: الأول اتصال مواد الوحي به، ويؤيد ذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿ مَا وَدَعَكَ رَبُّكَ وَمَا قَلَى ﴾ [الضحى : ٣] والثاني – تنبيه عن مواقع الزلل مثل قوله تعالى : عَفَا اللَّهُ عَنكَ لِمَ أَذِنتَ لَهُمْ ﴾ [التوبة: ٤٣] . والخواص كلها بأقسامها توفرت في نبينا محمد .
And after that he speaks about the special properties (khaṣāʾiṣ) of prophethood and summarizes them in two divisions. The first: for preparing its affair and consolidating its foundation. The second: for nurturing its powers. And he divides the first into two: one of them is the genetic choice (al-ikhtiyār al-jinsī), in which nobility (al-sharaf) is present. The second: the presence of virtuous powers (al-quwā al-fāḍila) in him, and the removal of defects (al-ʿilal) from him; for he was perfect in intellect (al-ʿaql), character (al-khuluq), and physique (al-khilqa). As for the second division, he divides it into two: the first is the connection of the materials of revelation (mawādd al-waḥy) to him, and that is supported by His statement, exalted is He: 'Your Lord has not forsaken you, nor has He hated [you]' (Q 93:3). The second is alerting to places of stumbling (mawāqiʿ al-zalal), such as His statement, exalted is He: 'May Allah pardon you, [O Muḥammad]; why did you give them permission [to stay behind]?' (Q 9:43). And all the special properties, with their divisions, were fully present in our Prophet Muḥammad.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage classifies the special characteristics (khaṣāʾiṣ) of prophethood into two main categories. The first category aims to establish and consolidate the foundation of prophethood; it includes two elements: (a) the Prophet's noble lineage (genetic choice) and (b) his perfection in intellect, character, and physical form, free from defects. The second category aims to nurture the powers of prophethood; it also includes two elements: (a) the continuous connection to revelation, as confirmed by Q 93:3 that God did not abandon him, and (b) divine correction for any missteps, as in Q 9:43 where God gently reproaches him for permitting some to stay behind. The passage concludes that all these properties were fully realized in the Prophet Muḥammad.

Key Terms
خواص النبوة
تمهيد
تربية القوى
الاختيار الجنسي
الشرف
القوى الفاضلة
العلل
اتصال مواد الوحي
تنبيه عن مواقع الزلل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The second category (nurturing powers) implies that the Prophet had deficiencies that needed correction.
Correction: The second category actually shows divine care and training, not deficiency. The Prophet was perfect; these are aspects of his prophetic mission.

Checkpoint
Into how many main divisions does Nasafi categorize the special properties of prophethood?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Nasafi teaches that prophethood's special properties encompass both foundational perfection (lineage and virtues) and nurturant care (revelation and correction), all perfectly embodied in the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that the Prophet, despite his perfection, was divinely corrected in matters like giving permission to the hypocrites. When was the last time you humbly accepted a correction from someone, or from Allah through His verses? Are you open to being alerted to your own 'places of stumbling' even when it is uncomfortable? What would it take for you to embrace correction as a form of divine care rather than a sign of failure?
?
The passage highlights that the Prophet had a noble lineage and perfect virtues. Do you ever envy the Prophet's perfection, or do you use it as a model for your own growth? In what area of your life—intellect, character, or physique—are you most neglecting to strive towards excellence? What concrete step will you take this week to improve one of these three?
?
The 'connection of revelation materials' ensured the Prophet was never forsaken. Do you truly believe that Allah has not forsaken you, even in your darkest moments? Or do you harbor a secret fear that He has abandoned you due to your sins? Read Q 93:3 again—allow it to pierce your heart. How would your life change today if you fully trusted that your Lord has not hated you?

Nasafi's Apology for Lengthy Prophethood
Nasafi apologizes for lengthy prophethood discussion, cites atheism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi chose to write extensively on prophethood despite his methodological commitment.

Core Idea
Lengthy discussion is justified by the need to combat widespread atheism.

This brief passage serves as Nasafi's concluding remark on prophethood. He acknowledges his deviation from the concise methodology he initially set for himself, but he provides a compelling reason: the rampant atheism of his time, even affecting caliphs. This lesson examines his apology and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation to get the gist.
Notice the author's apologetic tone.
2
Identify the two elements
Find the apology for prolixity and the reason given. The passage has two clear parts: the apology and the justification.
The reason is explicitly stated: the spread of atheism.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why a theologian would need to address contemporary challenges. This shows that scholarly works respond to their context.
Think about how this applies to other theological debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويختم كلامه في النبوة معتذرا عن الإطالة التي أخرجته عن المنهج الذي اشترطه إلا أنه يبين السبب الدافع إلى ذلك وهو الإلحاد الذي يقول عنه: (إنه تفشى في زمانه وطعن بعض الخلفاء في أمور النبوة).
And he concludes his speech on prophethood, apologizing for the prolixity that removed him from the methodology (al-minhāj) that he had stipulated. However, he explains the driving reason for that, which is atheism (al-ilḥād) about which he says: 'It has spread in his time, and some of the caliphs (al-khulafāʾ) attacked matters of prophethood.'
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This brief passage serves as a concluding note to the section on prophethood. The author acknowledges that his discussion was longer than intended, deviating from the self-imposed methodology. He justifies this by citing the widespread atheism (ilḥād) in his time, and specifically that some caliphs even attacked matters related to prophethood. Thus, the extended treatment was necessary to address these challenges.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Nasafi's lengthy discussion was a mistake or lack of planning.
Correction: Nasafi deliberately expanded due to the pressing need to address atheism, as he states.

Three Categories of People
Nasafi enumerates three categories of people.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three main categories of people based on their intellectual capacity and worldly pursuits as described by Imam al-Nasafi.

Core Idea
People are divided by intellect and focus: seekers of truth, seekers of world, and the dull.

Imam al-Nasafi begins by classifying humanity according to their intellectual ability and life orientation. He identifies three groups: those with acute minds who investigate realities, those occupied with worldly gains, and those with dull understanding. This classification sets the stage for understanding how divine mercy reaches each group.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Note the structure: second type first, then first division with two subgroups.
2
Identify the three groups
List the three groups: those with dull understanding, those devoted to truth, and those occupied with worldly means.
Notice that the first type is divided into two.
3
Reflect on the descriptions
Consider the language: 'extracting deposits of intellects' vs 'content with the rank of animals'. What does this tell you about their priorities?
The contrast highlights different levels of aspiration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأذهان. والثاني: الموصوفون بغلظ الأفهام وبلادة الخواطر. والقسم الأول فرقتان أحدهما المتفرغة للتأمل والتفكر والبحث عن الحقائق واليقين، سمت بهم همتهم إلى استخراج ودائع العقول وخزائن الأفهام، والوقوف على ما به الفوز لهم بالسعادة الأبدية، والوصول إلى مرضاة خالق البرية جل وتعالى. والأخرى من الفريقين المشتغلة باكتساب أسباب المعاش، المعرضة عن التأمل في المعالم النظرية، الراضية لنفسها درجة البهائم، لاقتصارها على استجلاب اللذات الحاضرة، ونيل شهواتها الطبيعية المقبلة على تكثير الأموال النفيسة، والعقود الخطيرة بأنواع التجارات، وصنوف الزراعات. ثم إن الله تعالى ترحم على الناس كافة ببعث الرسول، وبيان ما يحتاجون إليه في الدارين، فكانت مرحمته تعالى لهم في القسم الذي ليس في قوة العقول الوقوف عليها بإثبات طريق الوصول في حق طبقات الناس كلهم ورحمته تعالى وتفضله في حق القسم الذي العقول إمكان الوقوف عليه في حق الموصوفين بكمال العقول وحدة الخواطر والأذهان، المتفرغين للبحث عن الحقائق، بتسهيل سبيل الوصول، والتنبيه لكيفية الاستدلال، وفي حق الموصوفين بالبلادة وغلظ الأفهام بإثبات طريق الوصول. وكذا في حق المعرضين عن طلب الحقائق المشتغلين باكتساب أسباب المعاش، فمن يثبت من هؤلاء في حقه معجزة الرسول بالمشاهدة أو بالنقل المتواتر الذي يضاهي المتصل به الثابت بالمشاهدة، كان قول الرسول في حق طريق الوصول إلى ثبوته عنده، وإن لم يوجد منه الاستدلال العقلي يجعل الله تعالى ذلك الطريق في حقة كجملة دلائل العقول سبيل الوصول في حق غيره، مرحمة منه على هؤلاء الضعفة، وتخفيفا للمؤنة عنهم وتيسيرا عليهم.
And the second: those described with thickness of understanding and dullness of minds. And the first division is two groups: one of them devoted to reflection, contemplation, and investigation of realities and certainty; their ambition elevated them to extract the deposits of intellects and treasures of understandings, and to attain what leads to eternal happiness and reaching the pleasure of the Creator of creation, glorified and exalted. And the other of the two groups is occupied with acquiring means of livelihood, turning away from reflection in theoretical matters, content with the rank of animals, because they restrict themselves to procuring immediate pleasures and attaining their natural desires, focused on multiplying precious wealth and significant contracts through various types of trades and kinds of agriculture. Then Allah, exalted, showed mercy to all people by sending the Messenger and explaining what they need in both abodes. So His mercy to them in the category that the power of intellects cannot comprehend was by establishing a way of access for all classes of people. And His mercy and favor in the category that intellects have the ability to comprehend was in the case of those described with complete intellects, sharpness of thoughts and minds, devoted to investigating realities, by facilitating the way of access and alerting to the method of reasoning. And similarly for those described with dullness and thickness of understanding by establishing a way of access. And likewise for those turning away from seeking realities, occupied with acquiring means of livelihood. So whoever among these verifies for himself a miracle of the Messenger through direct observation or through mutawatir transmission that is like direct confirmation, then the word of the Messenger regarding the way of access to its establishment for him, even if rational deduction is not present from him, Allah makes that way for him like the totality of intellectual proofs as a way of access in the case of others, as mercy from Him upon these weak ones, and an alleviation of burden and an easing for them.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage classifies people and explains God's mercy in providing a way to truth for each type. The author first mentions the second type: those with dull understanding (غلظ الأفهام وبلادة الخواطر). Then he discusses the first type, which is divided into two subgroups. The first subgroup devotes itself to reflection and investigation of realities, aiming for eternal happiness and God's pleasure. The second subgroup, by contrast, is occupied with earning a livelihood and pursuing worldly pleasures, content with a rank like that of animals. The author then explains that God's mercy sent the Prophet to all people. For the category that intellects cannot grasp (i.e., matters of the unseen), God establishes a way of access (طريق الوصول) for all classes. For those with sharp intellects, God facilitates the way through rational deduction (الاستدلال العقلي). For those with dullness, God provides a way via miracles. Specifically, if a person witnesses a miracle directly or through reliable transmission (النقل المتواتر), the Prophet's word becomes a sufficient way of access for that person, even without rational deduction. This is a mercy and alleviation from God.

Key Terms
العقول
الفهم
الخواطر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all people are equally capable of rational deduction.
Correction: The passage shows different categories, each with distinct capacities and orientations.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which group is described as 'content with the rank of animals'?
A) Those with dull understanding
B) Those devoted to reflection
C) Those occupied with acquiring means of livelihood
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
People vary in intellectual ability and life focus, and Islam recognizes these differences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
As you read this classification, which of these three descriptions (dull, reflective seeker, worldly seeker) most accurately describes you right now? What is one concrete change you can make today to move toward being among the reflective seekers?
?
The worldly group is said to be content with the rank of animals because they pursue only immediate pleasures. Is there any area of your life—your work, relationships, or habits—where you are prioritizing short-term satisfaction over eternal happiness? What would it cost you to shift your focus?
?
The reflective group extracts deposits of intellects and aims for God's pleasure. What is one deep question about your faith or purpose that you have been avoiding or procrastinating? Commit to investigating it this week, even if only for fifteen minutes.

God's Mercy Through the Messenger
Nasafi details God's mercy in providing access to truth for all human categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how God's mercy provides a path to truth for every type of person through the Prophet's mission.

Core Idea
God's mercy sends the Prophet to guide all: reason, miracle, or acceptance of the message.

After classifying people, Imam al-Nasafi now explains the all-encompassing mercy of God in sending the Messenger. For those with sharp intellects, rational deduction is facilitated; for those who cannot reason, miracles and reliable transmission establish the truth. The Prophet's word becomes a sufficient proof, even without rational deduction, out of mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the mercy passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the section starting from 'ثم إن الله تعالى ترحم'. Pay attention to the different categories mentioned.
2
Identify the four ways of access
The passage mentions four categories within the mercy: those who cannot reason, those with sharp intellects, those with dullness, and those occupied with world. For each, note the means: establishment of a way, facilitation of reasoning, establishment via miracles, and acceptance of the Prophet's word.
The last group relies on witnessing a miracle.
3
Understand the role of miracles and transmission
The text links miracles to direct observation or mutawatir transmission. This is a key theological concept: reliable transmission has the force of direct evidence.
4
Ponder the mercy and alleviation
The passage ends with 'mercy upon these weak ones' and 'alleviation of burden'. Reflect on how this shows God's compassion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأذهان. والثاني: الموصوفون بغلظ الأفهام وبلادة الخواطر. والقسم الأول فرقتان أحدهما المتفرغة للتأمل والتفكر والبحث عن الحقائق واليقين، سمت بهم همتهم إلى استخراج ودائع العقول وخزائن الأفهام، والوقوف على ما به الفوز لهم بالسعادة الأبدية، والوصول إلى مرضاة خالق البرية جل وتعالى. والأخرى من الفريقين المشتغلة باكتساب أسباب المعاش، المعرضة عن التأمل في المعالم النظرية، الراضية لنفسها درجة البهائم، لاقتصارها على استجلاب اللذات الحاضرة، ونيل شهواتها الطبيعية المقبلة على تكثير الأموال النفيسة، والعقود الخطيرة بأنواع التجارات، وصنوف الزراعات. ثم إن الله تعالى ترحم على الناس كافة ببعث الرسول، وبيان ما يحتاجون إليه في الدارين، فكانت مرحمته تعالى لهم في القسم الذي ليس في قوة العقول الوقوف عليها بإثبات طريق الوصول في حق طبقات الناس كلهم ورحمته تعالى وتفضله في حق القسم الذي العقول إمكان الوقوف عليه في حق الموصوفين بكمال العقول وحدة الخواطر والأذهان، المتفرغين للبحث عن الحقائق، بتسهيل سبيل الوصول، والتنبيه لكيفية الاستدلال، وفي حق الموصوفين بالبلادة وغلظ الأفهام بإثبات طريق الوصول. وكذا في حق المعرضين عن طلب الحقائق المشتغلين باكتساب أسباب المعاش، فمن يثبت من هؤلاء في حقه معجزة الرسول بالمشاهدة أو بالنقل المتواتر الذي يضاهي المتصل به الثابت بالمشاهدة، كان قول الرسول في حق طريق الوصول إلى ثبوته عنده، وإن لم يوجد منه الاستدلال العقلي يجعل الله تعالى ذلك الطريق في حقة كجملة دلائل العقول سبيل الوصول في حق غيره، مرحمة منه على هؤلاء الضعفة، وتخفيفا للمؤنة عنهم وتيسيرا عليهم.
And the second: those described with thickness of understanding and dullness of minds. And the first division is two groups: one of them devoted to reflection, contemplation, and investigation of realities and certainty; their ambition elevated them to extract the deposits of intellects and treasures of understandings, and to attain what leads to eternal happiness and reaching the pleasure of the Creator of creation, glorified and exalted. And the other of the two groups is occupied with acquiring means of livelihood, turning away from reflection in theoretical matters, content with the rank of animals, because they restrict themselves to procuring immediate pleasures and attaining their natural desires, focused on multiplying precious wealth and significant contracts through various types of trades and kinds of agriculture. Then Allah, exalted, showed mercy to all people by sending the Messenger and explaining what they need in both abodes. So His mercy to them in the category that the power of intellects cannot comprehend was by establishing a way of access for all classes of people. And His mercy and favor in the category that intellects have the ability to comprehend was in the case of those described with complete intellects, sharpness of thoughts and minds, devoted to investigating realities, by facilitating the way of access and alerting to the method of reasoning. And similarly for those described with dullness and thickness of understanding by establishing a way of access. And likewise for those turning away from seeking realities, occupied with acquiring means of livelihood. So whoever among these verifies for himself a miracle of the Messenger through direct observation or through mutawatir transmission that is like direct confirmation, then the word of the Messenger regarding the way of access to its establishment for him, even if rational deduction is not present from him, Allah makes that way for him like the totality of intellectual proofs as a way of access in the case of others, as mercy from Him upon these weak ones, and an alleviation of burden and an easing for them.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage classifies people and explains God's mercy in providing a way to truth for each type. The author first mentions the second type: those with dull understanding (غلظ الأفهام وبلادة الخواطر). Then he discusses the first type, which is divided into two subgroups. The first subgroup devotes itself to reflection and investigation of realities, aiming for eternal happiness and God's pleasure. The second subgroup, by contrast, is occupied with earning a livelihood and pursuing worldly pleasures, content with a rank like that of animals. The author then explains that God's mercy sent the Prophet to all people. For the category that intellects cannot grasp (i.e., matters of the unseen), God establishes a way of access (طريق الوصول) for all classes. For those with sharp intellects, God facilitates the way through rational deduction (الاستدلال العقلي). For those with dullness, God provides a way via miracles. Specifically, if a person witnesses a miracle directly or through reliable transmission (النقل المتواتر), the Prophet's word becomes a sufficient way of access for that person, even without rational deduction. This is a mercy and alleviation from God.

Key Terms
الاستدلال العقلي
المعجزة
النقل المتواتر
طريق الوصول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That only rational argument is valid for establishing truth.
Correction: The author shows multiple paths: reason, miracles, and acceptance of prophetic testimony.

B) Those who verify a miracle through direct observation or mutawatir transmission
C) Those who reject all proofs
D) Only the Prophet himself

Key Takeaway
God's mercy ensures that no one is left without a path to truth, whether through reason, miracle, or acceptance of prophetic testimony.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage reveals that God provides different paths to truth for different people. Which path do you actually rely on: your own reasoning, acceptance of miracles, or humble submission to the Prophet's words? Are you proud of your intellect or using it as a shield against surrender?
?
You likely do not witness miracles firsthand, but you claim to believe in those reported through mutawatir transmission. Does this belief truly guide your daily actions, or do you treat it as mere historical fact? If the Prophet's word is sufficient even without rational proof, why do you still seek intellectual loopholes to avoid full commitment?
?
Are you among those 'occupied with acquiring means of livelihood'? How does this passage expose your excuses for not prioritizing the pursuit of truth? What would you change today if you truly believed that a simple miracle story could be your enough path to God?

Refutation of Those Who Demand Rational Deduction
The author refutes insistence on rational deduction by citing the Prophet's practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why rational deduction is not a necessary condition for faith, as demonstrated by the Prophet's practice with the unlettered Arabs.

Core Idea
The Prophet's mission to an unlettered nation shows that miracles and the Quran suffice for belief.

This lesson examines a key argument from Imam al-Nasafi against those who insist on formal rational deduction as a prerequisite for faith. The author points to the actual practice of the Prophet and early Muslims, who accepted faith based on direct experience of miracles and the Quran's inimitability, not deductive reasoning. The passage challenges the notion that theological reasoning is the only path to belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage deliberately
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the author's central claim and the proof he provides.
The Arabic uses a compressed style; the translation will clarify the argument.
2
Identify the author's premise and proof
Locate the statement that those who require rational deduction oppose God's wisdom. Then find the proof (daliil): the practice of the Prophet, caliphs, and imams.
3
Examine the description of the unlettered nation
Notice how the author describes the Arabs: they lacked deductive skills, worshipped idols, rejected tawhid, and found resurrection and a human messenger impossible.
This sets up the need for an alternative to rational deduction.
4
Understand how belief occurred
The passage explains that when they witnessed miracles or heard the Quran and recognized its inimitability, they believed. This shows that direct experience of divine signs sufficed.
The author does not claim that rational deduction is useless, only that it is not always required.
5
Reflect on the lesson's implication
Consider how this argument defends the universality of the Prophet's message. The condition of rational deduction would exclude many people, contradicting God's mercy.
This connects to the broader theme of God's wisdom in sending messengers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان في الجملة في عقولهم إمكان الوقوف على ذلك، فمن لم يرض بهذا، وشرط الاستدلال العقلي هذا فقد عارض الله سبحانه وتعالى في حكمته وضاده فيما أنعم به على الضعفة مع من عباده من آثار رحمته ودليل هذه المقدمة أنه جعل قول الرسول في حق هؤلاء طريق الوصول وإن لم يوجد منهم الاستدلال العقلي صنيع الرسول وضيع الخلفاء الراشدين بعده، وصنيع جميع أئمة المسلمين وسلاطينهم إلى يومنا هذا. أما صنيع الرسول فإنه بعث في الأمة الأمية الخالية عن صناعة الاستدلال، والعلم بشرائطه، كل منهم يعبدون ما ينحتون ويعتقدون أن ما يعبده أهل قبيلته وجملة أقاربه وعشيرته من الصنم المنحوت من الصخر والخشب شريك لله تعالى، وكانوا يتعجبون من تجريد التوحيد، وخلع الأنداد، ويقولون للرسول: أَجَعَلَ الْأَلِمَةَ إِلَها وَاحِدًا إِنَّ هَذَا لَشَيْءٍ عُجَابٌ وكانوا يرون البعث والنشور ممتنعا حتى قالوا: مَن يُحْيِ الْعِظَمَ وَهِيَ رَمِيمٌ وبعث الله تعالى بشرا رسولا مستحيلا على ما أخبره الله تعالى فقال: وَمَا مَنَعَ النَّاسَ أَن يُؤْمِنُوا إِذْ جَاءَهُمُ الْهُدَى إِلَّا أَن قَالُوا أَبَعَتَ اللهُ بَشَرًا رَّسُولًا ثم إن واحدا منهم إذا عاين معجزة ناقضة للعادة أو سمع القرآن وعرف وجه إعجازه لمعرفته بجواهر الكلام، وصنوف البلاغة، وضروب النظم، ثم رأي القرآن باين كلا في النظم، وفاق جميعها في الفصاحة والبلاغة، فاعترف برسالته، وأقر
Although in general there is possibility in their intellects to comprehend that, whoever is not satisfied with this and stipulates rational deduction, then he has opposed Allah, glorified and exalted, in His wisdom and antagonized Him in what He bestowed upon the weak among His servants of the effects of His mercy. And the proof of this premise is that He made the word of the Messenger for these people a way of access even if rational deduction is not present from them, [as is evident from] the practice of the Messenger and the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs after him, and the practice of all the imams of the Muslims and their sultans up to our present day. As for the practice of the Messenger: he was sent to the unlettered nation, devoid of the art of deduction and knowledge of its conditions; each of them worshipped what they carve [from stone], and believed that what the people of his tribe and all his relatives and clan worshipped of the idol carved from rock and wood is a partner of Allah, exalted. And they used to marvel at the stripping of tawhid and removal of rivals, and said to the Messenger: 'Has he made the gods one God? Indeed, this is a strange thing.' And they considered resurrection and gathering impossible until they said: 'Who will give life to bones while they are decayed?' And they considered it impossible that Allah would send a human as a messenger, as Allah informed, saying: 'And what prevented the people from believing when guidance came to them except that they said: Has Allah sent a human as a messenger?' Then when one of them witnessed a miracle breaking custom or heard the Quran and recognized the aspect of its inimitability due to his knowledge of the gems of speech, types of eloquence, and varieties of composition, and then saw the Quran surpassing all others in composition, excelling all of them in eloquence and rhetoric, he acknowledged his messengership and affirmed...
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage refutes those who demand rational deduction as a prerequisite for faith. The author argues that if someone is not satisfied with the messenger's word and requires rational deduction, they are opposing God's wisdom and mercy. The proof (دليل هذه المقدمة) is the practice of the Prophet, the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and all Muslim imams and rulers. The author elaborates on the Prophet's practice: he was sent to an unlettered nation (الأمة الأمية) that had no knowledge of deductive reasoning. They worshipped idols, rejected the oneness of God, and found the idea of resurrection impossible. They also objected to a human messenger. Yet, when they witnessed a miracle breaking custom (معجزة ناقضة للعادة) or heard the Quran and recognized its inimitability (إعجاز) due to their understanding of eloquence, they believed. This shows that for such people, direct experience of the miracle or the Quran was sufficient, and rational deduction was not required. The author thus demonstrates that imposing a condition of rational deduction contradicts the universal mercy of God, who provided a way for all to believe.

الأمة الأمية

Correction: The Prophet's practice with the unlettered shows that witnessing miracles or the Quran is sufficient for faith, and requiring rational deduction contradicts God's wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author says that insisting on rational deduction opposes Allah's wisdom and mercy. In what area of your life are you demanding a logical answer from Allah before you obey, even though He has already given you clear signs? Will you today submit to His mercy and accept His messenger's way, even if your intellect cannot fully grasp it?

The Absurdity of Denying Prophetic Evidence for God
Refutes absurd consequences of claiming prophetic testimony is insufficient evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that prophetic speech is not valid evidence for God's existence is self-refuting and leads to impossible consequences.

Core Idea
Denying prophetic evidence leads to absurdities that even madmen recognize.

The author presents a powerful reductio ad absurdum argument. If we accept the claim that the Prophet's word cannot serve as evidence for God's existence and the world's creation, then the Prophet would be guilty of serious failures—being mistaken, deficient, lying, and deserving eternal punishment. Such a consequence is obviously corrupt, proving the original claim is false. This lesson walks through that argument, showing how rational consistency demands accepting prophetic testimony as valid evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation. Notice how the author builds a chain of consequences from a single premise.
Pay attention to the emotional force of the language (e.g., 'not hidden from madmen').
2
Identify the absurd consequences
The passage lists several impossible outcomes if the Prophet's word were not evidence. List them: the Prophet would be mistaken, deficient, lying, etc.
These are meant to be clearly unacceptable.
3
Understand the logical structure
The author states a general principle: every rational argument that leads to corruption is itself corrupt. The opponent's claim leads to corruption, so it is corrupt.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Ask yourself: why does this refutation work? Because it shows the opponent's position entails a self-contradiction: the Prophet would be both a messenger and a liar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بإيمانهم كان مخطئا في الحكم بإيمانهم مقصرا في أداء ما أرد بأدائه إلى الناس، غير مبلغ ما وجب عليه تبليغه، كاذبا في دعواه التبليغ، مرتكبا المآثم في الامتناع عن التبليغ على وجه يصير من اتبعه مؤمنا خارجا عن الإيمان بارتكابه هذه الكبيرة وهي الامتناع عن التبليغ على مذهبهم مستحقا الخلود في النار، وكل قول هذا عقباه ففساده لا يخفى على المجانين فضلا عن العقلاء، وما اعتمده من الدليل أن قول الرسول لا يصلح دليلا لثبوت الصانع وحدوث العالم، يفضي إلى هذه المعاني المستحيلة، وكل معقول يؤدي إلى فساد فهو فاسد، فكذا هذا.
He was mistaken in judging their faith, deficient in delivering what he intended to deliver to the people, not conveying what was obligatory for him to convey, lying in his claim of conveyance, committing sins by refraining from conveyance in a way that makes those who follow him believers, exiting from faith by committing this major sin—which is refraining from conveyance according to their doctrine—deserving eternal punishment in Hell. And every statement whose consequence is such, its corruption is not hidden from madmen, let alone the rational. And what he relied on as evidence—that the Prophet's speech is not valid as evidence for establishing the Maker and the temporality of the world—leads to these impossible meanings. And every rational argument that leads to corruption is itself corrupt. So too is this.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is a refutation. It begins by describing the absurd consequences of the opposing view: if the Prophet's word is not sufficient evidence, then the Prophet would be considered mistaken, deficient, lying, and deserving eternal punishment. Then it argues that such a view is obviously corrupt, even to madmen. The opponent's reliance on the claim that the Prophet's speech is not evidence for God's existence and the world's creation leads to impossible outcomes. The author concludes that any rational argument that leads to corruption is itself corrupt, and thus the opponent's claim is corrupt.

حدوث العالم
دليل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: Some think that rejecting prophetic evidence is a sophisticated intellectual stance.
Correction: The author shows that this stance leads to self-contradiction: the Prophet would be both a truthful messenger and a liar, which is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The claim that prophetic testimony cannot prove God's existence is self-refuting because it would imply the Prophet is a liar and deserving of hell, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The lesson shows that rejecting prophetic evidence leads to absurd consequences, including the Prophet being a liar. When you ignore or downplay a command from the Sunnah, are you not, in practice, implying that the Prophet's testimony is insufficient? How would you respond if you were to be confronted with that implication on the Day of Judgment?
?
Imagine that you are like the madmen who can see the corruption of this argument—yet you still find yourself hesitating to submit fully to the prophetic message. What is holding you back? Ask Allah to remove that barrier and commit to acting on one specific prophetic teaching today, no matter how small.

The Prophet's Call and Knowledge from Miracles
Nasafi explains the prophetic call and the epistemological status of belief based on miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in a prophet's message, when confirmed by a miracle, constitutes certain knowledge, regardless of whether the believer understands the mechanics of the proof.

Core Idea
A miracle transforms a prophet's message into undeniable knowledge.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi describes how a prophet presents his message and demonstrates his truthfulness through a miracle. The one who witnesses the miracle or learns of it through tawatur gains certain knowledge of the prophet's truthfulness, even if he cannot articulate how the miracle proves it. This lesson establishes that such belief is genuine knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the prophet's presentation
Read the passage where the prophet explains his message and provides a miracle. Notice the comprehensive nature of the teaching.
The prophet explains tawhid, his prophethood, and obligations.
2
Identify the role of the miracle
The miracle is the evidence that confirms the prophet's truthfulness. The passage emphasizes that it is beyond human capacity and breaks custom.
3
Understand tawatur
The called person may learn of the miracle through tawatur (mass transmission), which also yields certainty.
Tawatur ensures reliable transmission.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that ignorance of how the miracle indicates truth does not negate knowledge, because the belief is established on a solid foundation.
This is a key point about the nature of knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

على عباده كذا ونهاني عن كذا، ثم جعل هذا الناقض للعادة، الخارج عن وسع الخلق دليلا على صدقي، وشاهد هذا المدعو المعجزة أو دعا بعض أئمة الأمة وعرف المدعو ثبوت المعجزة بالتواتر، فصدقه هذا المدعو، و اعتقد إنه حكيم لا يقيم الدلالة على يدي المتنبي، أو هو كامل القدرة لا يتصور عجزه عن إثبات التفرقة بين الحق والباطل والجهل بكيفية دلالة الدليل يوجب خروج اعتقاده عن كونه علما، لثبوته على وجه ينافي جميع أضداد العلم لا ويجلي له المعلوم كعامي رأى بناء فاعتقد أن له بانيا، كان اعتقاده علما، لأنه بناه على الدليل إذ البناء دليل الباني، وإن كان لا يعرف كيفية دلالة الدليل، وهي أن البناء لما كان يتصور أن يكون أعلى من هذا أو أسفل، وأغلظ منه أو أدق، وأوثق منه أو أوهى، وأحسن منه أو أردأ، وكان من الجائز أن يكون على هذا فاختصاصه بهذا الوجه الذي هو عليه مع جواز أن لا يكون عليه بل يكون على غيره لن يكون إلا بتخصيص مخصص قادر مختار، وجهله بكيفية هذه الدلالة لا تخرج عقيدته من أن تكون علما، فكذا هذا يحققه أن الخصوم ساعدوا على هذا وقالوا بمثله فإن عندي الأشعري لو عرف دليلا واحدا في كل مسألة وبنى عليه اعتقاده، ثم وردت عليه شبهة عجز عن دفعها ولم يتزلزل اعتقاده بل بقى متقررا على ما اعتقده معتقدا أن تلك شبهة لا حجة، وأن وراءها من يدفعها من متكلمي أهل الإسلام، بقي مؤمنا وإن كان تعارض الأدلة يخرج الرأي عن حد العلم إلى الظن والشك والوقوف ولكن لما كان هذا الرجل بقي بانيا اعتقاده على دليل موجب للعلم، واعتقد تلك الشبهة باطلة كان اعتقاده علما لكونه مبنيا على دليل موجب للعلم وإن كان لا يهتدي إلى جهة بطلان الشبهة، وكيفية دلالة دليله على بطلان الشبهة فكذا هذا، وكذا عند المعتزلة من وجد منهم شرط صحة إيمانه وحكم له بالإيمان ثم اعترضت عليه بعد ذلك شبهة ولم يكن عنده من الجواب ما به يوجب دفعها لانعدام هذه الشبهة على خاطره فيما مضى من الأزمنة، ويحتاج إلى التأمل فيها ليقف على وجه دفعها لم يبطل إيمانه في هذه المدة، وإن تعارضت الأدلة ولم يهتد إلى كيفية وجه الدفع، ولكن لما اعتقد صحة دينه بانيا اعتقاده على دليل واعتقد بطلانها عن دليل يوجب بطلانها كان اعتقاده علما ينافي جميع أضداده ويتجلى
Then we say: When the Prophet calls someone to his religion, he explains to him all that concerns his belief, saying: This world is temporally originated, has one Creator, no partner, no likeness, described with attributes of perfection, free from traits of deficiency, and that He sent me as a messenger, and obligated on His servants such and such, and prohibited such and such. Then he makes this miracle—which breaks custom and is beyond human capacity—as evidence of my truthfulness. And this caller witnesses the miracle, or perhaps some imams of the community call and the called person knows the miracle through tawatur. So he believes him and believes all that he called him to based on news; and the news of one whose truthfulness is proven by a miracle is a cause for the establishment of knowledge. Thus the man builds his belief in all that he was called to on what is evidence, except that he does not know the manner of the miracle's indication of the truthfulness of its bringer—which is our statement: He (God) is wise, He does not set up evidence through a false prophet, or He is perfect in power, His inability to distinguish between truth and falsehood is inconceivable. And ignorance of the manner of the indication of the evidence does not necessitate that his belief ceases to be knowledge, because it is established in a way that contradicts all opposites of knowledge. And it clarifies for him the known (object), like a commoner who saw a building and believed it has a builder; his belief was knowledge because he built it on evidence, since the building is evidence of the builder, even if he does not know the manner of the evidence's indication—namely, that the building could be higher or lower, thicker or thinner, stronger or weaker, better or worse, and it is possible that it be such; so its being specifically in that way, given the possibility that it could be otherwise, can only be due to the specification of a powerful, free chooser. And his ignorance of the manner of this indication does not take his belief out of being knowledge. So too this. And it is confirmed that the opponents agreed on this and said the like. For according to Ash'ari: If a person knew one proof in every issue and built his belief on it, then a counterargument came to him and he was unable to repel it, yet his belief did not waver but remained established on what he believed, considering that counterargument as no proof and that behind it someone from the Muslim theologians would repel it, he remains a believer. Even though conflicting arguments would remove opinion from the limit of knowledge to supposition, doubt, and suspension, but since this man remained building his belief on evidence necessitating knowledge and considered that counterargument false, his belief was knowledge because it was built on evidence necessitating knowledge, even if he could not find the way to refute the counterargument or the manner of his evidence's indication of the falsehood of the counterargument. So too this. And likewise according to the Mu'tazila: Whoever among them fulfills the condition of the validity of his faith and is judged to have faith, then a counterargument occurs to him afterwards and he has no answer by which to repel it, because this counterargument did not occur to his mind previously and he needs to reflect on it to find a way to repel it—his faith is not invalidated during this period. Even if the arguments conflict and he cannot find the manner of refutation, but since he believed the correctness of his religion building his belief on evidence and believed its falseness based on evidence necessitating its falsehood, his belief was knowledge that opposes all its opposites.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation and proof. It first describes how a prophet presents his message and provides a miracle. Then it explains that the believer's knowledge is built on that evidence, even without understanding how the miracle proves truthfulness. The analogy of the commoner and the building illustrates that one can have knowledge without knowing the detailed argument. Then it cites Ash'ari and Mu'tazila positions to show that even if counterarguments arise, faith remains knowledge if it is built on proper evidence.

Key Terms
معجزة
دليل
علم
تواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Knowledge requires understanding every step of the proof.
Correction: The passage shows that knowledge can be based on evidence even if one does not know how the evidence works.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does the called person come to know the miracle?
A) Only through direct witnessing
B) Only through tawatur
C) Either by witnessing or tawatur
D) Through rational deduction

Key Takeaway
Belief based on a miracle is knowledge even without understanding how the miracle proves truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson says that even if you do not understand how a miracle proves a prophet's truthfulness, your belief can still be certain knowledge. Think of a doctrine you believe but cannot fully explain. Are you willing to accept that your certainty can still be valid despite your lack of full understanding? What would it take for you to stop doubting that belief?
?
The prophet’s call began with explaining tawhid. When was the last time you examined your own understanding of tawhid not as a formula but as a living reality that shapes your daily decisions? What would change today if you acted as if Allah truly has no partner in your fears and hopes?
?
The passage treats knowledge from tawatur (widespread report) as equivalent to direct witness. Do you treat the miracles of the Prophet (like the splitting of the moon) with the same certainty as if you had seen them? If your conviction wavers, what does that reveal about the state of your faith? Consciously renew your faith in those reports today, not as stories, but as certain events that demand a response.

The Analogy of the Commoner and Scholarly Confirmation
Nasafi reinforces the nature of knowledge through analogy and scholarly consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that faith built on evidence remains knowledge even when confronted with unanswered objections, as illustrated by the analogy of the commoner and supported by Ash'ari and Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Evidence-based faith remains knowledge despite unanswered questions.

The passage uses a powerful analogy: a commoner who sees a building and knows it has a builder does not lose his knowledge even if he cannot explain the proof. Similarly, a believer may face counterarguments he cannot answer, yet his faith remains knowledge because it is built on solid evidence. Both Ash'ari and Mu'tazila scholars confirm this principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy of the commoner
Read how the commoner's belief in a builder is knowledge, and note the reasoning about specification.
The building's specific form necessitates a builder.
2
Apply the analogy to faith
The passage explicitly says 'so too this', linking the analogy to belief in the prophet.
3
Examine the Ash'ari position
Read how Ash'ari argues that a believer with one proof remains a believer even if a counterargument arises.
The believer remains confident that the objection is false.
4
Examine the Mu'tazila position
Read how Mu'tazila similarly hold that faith is not invalidated during reflection on a new objection.
Faith remains as long as it is based on evidence.

Source Text

ثم نقول: إن الرسول متى دعا أحدا إلى دينه يبين له جميع ما يعترض اعتقاده فيقول: إن هذا العالم محدث وله صانع واحد لا شريك له، ولا شبيه له موصوف بصفات الكمال متبرئ عن سمات النقص، وأنه بعثني رسولا، وأوجب على عباده كذا ونهاني عن كذا، ثم جعل هذا الناقض للعادة، الخارج عن وسع الخلق دليلا على صدقي، وشاهد هذا المدعو المعجزة أو دعا بعض أئمة الأمة وعرف المدعو ثبوت المعجزة بالتواتر، فصدقه هذا المدعو، و اعتقد جميع ما دعاه إليه بناء على خبر، وخبر من دلت المعجزة على صدقه سبب لثبوت العلم فيبني الرجل اعتقاده في جميع ما دعا إليه على ما هو دليل، غير أنه لا يعرف كيفية دلالة المعجزة على صدق الآتي بها وهو قولنا : ?

?

?

Do you have such trust in the tradition of Islamic scholarship? Or do you feel your faith depends on your own ability to answer every doubt? How does this affect your approach to learning?

Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
Ignorance of Definition Does Not Negate Knowledge
Nasafi argues that ignorance of definition does not negate knowledge, using analogy of two witnesses and applying to prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that knowledge is defined by firm conviction free from doubt, not by the ability to define knowledge or explain the proof in detail.

Core Idea
Knowledge is certainty of heart, not mastery of definitions.

In this passage, Nasafi addresses a potential objection: does a person need to know the precise definition of knowledge or the exact mechanism of proof in order to have true knowledge? He argues forcefully that it is the presence of certainty, free from doubt, that constitutes knowledge. Using a vivid analogy of two men hearing the same report from multiple witnesses, he shows that knowledge arises from the heart's settled conviction, not from intellectual analysis. He then applies this directly to the case of miracles and prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then the English translation. Pay attention to the flow of the argument.
The passage is dense but has a clear structure: principle, analogy, application.
2
Understand the main principle
Identify the opening statement: ignorance of the definition of knowledge does not negate knowledge when its cause exists. Notice the comparison with the commoner.
The key phrase is 'الجهل بتحديد العلم لا ينافي ثبوت العلم عند وجود سببه'.
3
Analyze the analogy of two men
Read the analogy carefully: two men hear a report from many witnesses. One's heart settles, the other's heart is disturbed. Understand why the first is considered knowledgeable and the second not.
The key factor is the presence or absence of doubt, not the report itself.
4
Apply the analogy to prophethood
See how Nasafi applies this to the miracle of a prophet: some people may doubt due to possible objections, while others have firm conviction. Only the latter have knowledge.
The same evidence is present for both, but doubt prevents knowledge.
5
Reflect on the takeaway
Consider the broader lesson: knowledge is defined by certainty free from doubt, not by the ability to articulate definitions or proofs.
This has implications for how we understand faith and knowledge in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فكذا هذا يحققه أن الجهل بتحديد العلم لا ينافي ثبوت العلم عند وجود سببه كما في حق العامي فكذا الجهل بكيفية دلالة الدليل لا ينافي العلم عند تحقيق دليله وسببه وخبر الصادق سبب العلم، وقد وقع له العلم به، فجهله بوجه الدلالة لا يخرجه من أن يكون علما، يحققه أن المنظور إليه حال من يقع له العلم فإن رجلين لو سمع كل واحد منهما خبرا من عشرة أو عشرين أو أكثر جاءوا من أماكن متفرقة في أزمنة مختلفة، فسكن قلب أحدهما إلى هذا الخبر، ووقع عنده أن لا تواطؤ يتوهم من هؤلاء، واضطرب قلب الآخر ووقع عنده أنهم ربما سبق منهم التواطؤ، كان الأول عالما والثاني لم يكن عالما فكذا فيما نحن فيه، نعتبر حال هذا الذي ثبت عنده المعجزة، فإن خطر بباله أن موجده ربما يكون سفيها يقيم الدليل على يد الكذاب، أو غير تام القدرة يجوز في حقه العجز عن التفرقة بين المحق والمبطل لم يكن هذا عالما بثبوت الرسالة وكون خبره دليلا للعلم قبل التأمل في جواز السفه والعجز على من أوجد الدلالة المعجزة، فأما من لم يخطر بباله هذا ولم يتردد قلبه واعتقد صدقه فقد اعتقد عن دليل فكان عالما، وخروج الأول عن كونه عالما، لا يوجب خروج هذا إذا سكن إليه واطمأن قلبه على صدق الآتي بها، وهذا لأن الدليل ثابت في حق كل واحد منهما إلا أن من اعترضت له شبهة فوقع له الشك وهو مناف للعلم ولا يثبت له العلم، ومن لم يثبت له الشك المنافي للعلم كان العلم ثابتا
So likewise, this is verified by the fact that ignorance of the definition of knowledge does not negate the establishment of knowledge when its cause exists, as in the case of the commoner. So likewise, ignorance of the manner of indication of the evidence does not negate knowledge when its evidence and cause are realized. And the truthful report is a cause of knowledge, and knowledge has occurred to him by it, so his ignorance of the aspect of indication does not remove it from being knowledge. It is verified that the consideration is the state of the one to whom knowledge occurs. For if two men heard a report from ten or twenty or more people who came from different places at different times, and the heart of one of them settled upon this report, and it occurred to him that no collusion is to be suspected from these, and the heart of the other was disturbed and it occurred to him that perhaps collusion preceded from them, the first is knowledgeable and the second is not knowledgeable. So likewise in our subject, we consider the state of this person for whom the miracle is established. If it occurs to his mind that its producer might be foolish, establishing evidence upon the hand of a liar, or not perfect in power such that inability to distinguish between the truthful and the false is permissible in His case, then this person is not knowledgeable of the establishment of prophethood and that his report is evidence for knowledge before reflecting on the permissibility of foolishness and inability upon the one who produced the evidential miracle. As for one for whom this does not occur to his mind and his heart does not waver and he believes his truthfulness, then he has believed upon evidence and so was knowledgeable. The exclusion of the first from being knowledgeable does not necessitate the exclusion of this one when he becomes calm and his heart feels secure upon the truthfulness of the one who brought it. And this is because the evidence is established for each one of them, except that the one for whom an objection arises, doubt occurs, which is contrary to knowledge, and knowledge is not established for him; and the one for whom doubt contrary to knowledge does not arise, knowledge is established.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage continues the argument by focusing on the irrelevance of knowing the formal definition of knowledge or the precise manner of proof (kayfiyyat al-dalala). Nasafi first states the principle: ignorance of the definition (tahdid al-'ilm) does not negate the existence of knowledge when its cause is present, as with the commoner. Then he provides a concrete analogy: two men hear the same report from many witnesses coming from different times and places. One's heart settles and he is convinced there is no collusion (tawatu'), while the other's heart is disturbed by doubt. The first has knowledge, the second does not. Applying this to the issue of prophethood: when a miracle is established, some people may entertain the possibility that the miracle's agent could be foolish or weak, thus doubting the truthfulness of the claimant. Such a person does not have knowledge of prophethood. But a person who does not entertain such doubts and whose heart settles on the truthfulness of the prophet has knowledge, built on evidence. The key point is that the evidence is the same for both, but the presence of doubt prevents knowledge for the first, while its absence allows knowledge for the second. Thus knowledge is defined by firm conviction free from doubt, not by explicit intellectual mastery of the proof.

Key Terms
علم
دليل
شبهة
معجزة
خبر صادق

Correction: Nasafi shows that knowledge is based on firm conviction free from doubt, not on the ability to articulate definitions or proofs.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge is firm conviction free from doubt, not the ability to define or prove.

Knowledge through Testimony: Doubt and Refutation
The author defends knowledge through testimony and refutes al-Jabba'i's inconsistency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that knowledge gained through testimony does not require explicit knowledge of the definition of knowledge or the modality of proof, and you will see the refutation of al-Jabba'i's inconsistency.

Core Idea
Ignorance of how proof works does not make knowledge invalid.

This lesson explores a key argument in epistemology of testimony: does one need to know the definition of knowledge or the precise way a proof indicates in order to have knowledge? The author argues no, using a vivid analogy of two listeners. He then applies this to the case of miracles and concludes by pointing out a contradiction in al-Jabba'i's position.

Guided Path
1
Understand the initial claim
The author states that ignorance of the definition of knowledge does not negate knowledge when its cause exists. Compare with the common person who knows something without defining it.
2
Follow the analogy of two listeners
Read the example of two men hearing testimony from many witnesses. One gains knowledge, the other does not due to doubt. Notice the key factor is the presence or absence of doubt.
3
Apply to the miracle case
The author applies the same reasoning to the one who witnesses a miracle. If he entertains doubts about God's wisdom or power, he does not gain knowledge. If not, he does.
4
Identify the refutation of al-Jabba'i
The author points out that al-Jabba'i's own definition of knowledge includes belief based on proof, yet he denies that belief in a miracle-supported report is knowledge, which is contradictory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
له به المعلوم فكذا هذا يحققه أن الجهل بتحديد العلم لا ينافي ثبوت العلم عند وجود سببه كما في حق العامي فكذا الجهل بكيفية دلالة الدليل لا ينافي العلم عند تحقيق دليله وسببه وخبر الصادق سبب العلم، وقد وقع له العلم به، فجهله بوجه الدلالة لا يخرجه من أن يكون علما، يحققه أن المنظور إليه حال من يقع له العلم فإن رجلين لو سمع كل واحد منهما خبرا من عشرة أو عشرين أو أكثر جاءوا من أماكن متفرقة في أزمنة مختلفة، فسكن قلب أحدهما إلى هذا الخبر، ووقع عنده أن لا تواطؤ يتوهم من هؤلاء، واضطرب قلب الآخر ووقع عنده أنهم ربما سبق منهم التواطؤ، كان الأول عالما والثاني لم يكن عالما فكذا فيما نحن فيه، نعتبر حال هذا الذي ثبت عنده المعجزة، فإن خطر بباله أن موجده ربما يكون سفيها يقيم الدليل على يد الكذاب، أو غير تام القدرة يجوز في حقه العجز عن التفرقة بين المحق والمبطل لم يكن هذا عالما بثبوت الرسالة وكون خبره دليلا للعلم قبل التأمل في جواز السفه والعجز على من أوجد الدلالة المعجزة، فأما من لم يخطر بباله هذا ولم يتردد قلبه واعتقد صدقه فقد اعتقد عن دليل فكان عالما، وخروج الأول عن كونه عالما، لا يوجب خروج هذا إذا سكن إليه واطمأن قلبه على صدق الآتي بها، وهذا لأن الدليل ثابت في حق كل واحد منهما إلا أن من اعترضت له شبهة فوقع له الشك وهو مناف للعلم ولا يثبت له العلم، ومن لم يثبت له الشك المنافي للعلم كان العلم ثابتا. فكذا هذا في حق من اعتمد الدليل إن لم يخطر بباله الشبهة المؤكدة للشك أو اعترضت ولم يلتفت إليها فلم يحصل له الشك المنافي للعلم حصل له العلم. ولو خطرت بباله الشبهة المولدة للشك، ووقع له الشك انتفى العلم عنه لوجود ما يضاده. على أن هذا من الجبائي مناقضة ظاهرة فإنه قال في تحديد العلم إنه اعتقاد الشيء على ما هو به عن ضرورة أو دليل، وهذا اعتقاد الشيء عن دليل لأن خبر المؤيد بالمعجزة دليل يوجب العلم ذلك لم يجعل هو هذا الاعتقاد علما، والله الموفق.
He verifies it: ignorance of the definition of knowledge does not negate the existence of knowledge when its cause exists, just as in the case of the common person. Likewise, ignorance of the modality of the indication of the proof does not negate knowledge when its proof and cause are realized. The report of the truthful one is a cause of knowledge, and knowledge has occurred to him by it. So his ignorance of the aspect of indication does not remove it from being knowledge. This is verified by considering the state of the one to whom knowledge occurs. For if two men each heard a report from ten or twenty or more people who came from different places at different times, and the heart of one of them settled upon this report, and it occurred to him that no collusion is conceivable from these people, while the heart of the other was disturbed and it occurred to him that they might have prearranged collusion, the first was knowledgeable and the second was not knowledgeable. Similarly in our case, we consider the state of the one for whom the miracle is established. If it occurs to his mind that its author might be a foolish one who establishes evidence upon the hand of a liar, or one not fully capable such that inability to distinguish between the truthful and the false is permissible in His right, then this one is not knowledgeable of the establishment of prophethood and that his report is a proof for knowledge, before reflecting on the permissibility of foolishness and incapacity upon the one who brought the miraculous evidence. But as for the one to whom this did not occur to his mind, and his heart did not waver, and he believed his truthfulness, then he has believed upon proof and thus was knowledgeable. The removal of the first from being knowledgeable does not necessitate the removal of this one if he settles and his heart is at peace with the truthfulness of the one who brought it. This is because the proof is established for each of them, except that the one who encountered a doubt and doubt occurred to him—and doubt is opposite to knowledge—knowledge is not established for him. And the one for whom the doubt opposite to knowledge did not occur, knowledge is established. So likewise in the case of the one who relies on the proof: if the doubt that reinforces doubt did not occur to his mind, or it occurred but he did not pay attention to it, so the doubt opposite to knowledge did not occur to him, knowledge occurs to him. And if the doubt that generates doubt occurred to his mind, and doubt occurred to him, knowledge is negated from him because of the existence of what opposes it. Moreover, this from al-Jabba'i is an apparent contradiction: for he said in the definition of knowledge that it is a belief of a thing as it is, out of necessity or proof, and this is a belief of a thing by proof, because the report supported by a miracle is a proof that necessitates knowledge, yet he did not make this belief knowledge. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument defending the possibility of knowledge through testimony (khabar) even when the recipient does not know the precise definition of knowledge or the modality of the proof. The author begins by noting that ignorance of the definition of knowledge does not prevent knowledge from occurring when its cause is present, comparing it to the common person. He then applies this to the modality of proof: ignorance of how the proof indicates does not negate knowledge. He illustrates with the example of two men hearing testimony from many witnesses: one is convinced of their truthfulness and gains knowledge, the other remains doubtful and does not. The author applies this to the case of miracles: the one who sees a miracle but entertains the possibility that God might be foolish or incapable does not attain knowledge of prophethood. The one who does not entertain such doubts and believes the prophet's truthfulness does so by proof and is knowledgeable. The author emphasizes that the proof is present for both, but doubt prevents knowledge. He then points out an inconsistency in al-Jabba'i, who defines knowledge as belief based on necessity or proof, yet denies that belief based on a miracle-supported report is knowledge, even though it is a proof that necessitates knowledge. The passage concludes with 'Allah is the Grantor of success.'

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ignorance of the definition of knowledge or the modality of proof makes knowledge impossible.
Correction: The author shows that knowledge can occur through testimony even if one does not understand the definition or how the proof works, as long as doubt does not arise.

Checkpoint
According to the analogy of the two listeners, what distinguishes the one who becomes knowledgeable from the one who does not?

B) The absence of doubt

Key Takeaway

?

Sacrifice as Proxy for Self-Sacrifice
Nasafi explains that sacrifices substitute for self-sacrifice as gratitude for existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why animal sacrifice is accepted as a proxy for self-sacrifice in gratitude for existence.

Core Idea
Sacrifice stands in for the life we owe in gratitude.

Why does Allah accept animal sacrifice instead of demanding our own lives? Imam Nasafi explains that the greatest gift—existence itself—calls for the greatest gratitude: offering our very being. But since that would end humanity, Allah in His wisdom instituted animal sacrifice as a substitute, following the example of Prophet Ishmael.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the analogy with wealth and fasting.
2
Identify the main claim
Nasafi states that sacrifices are a form of ransom for oneself. Find where he says that and note the underlying logic: gratitude for existence requires self-annihilation.
3
Follow the objection and solution
Why can't we actually sacrifice ourselves? The passage explains the consequence: humanity would end. Then see how Allah's wisdom provides a proxy.
This connects to the story of al-dhabih (Ishmael).
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Nasafi ends by saying this explanation is gratuitous. What does he mean? Consider that the religious obligation itself is sufficient without rational justification.
Think about the role of reason in worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم التقرب بالقرابين كل ذلك بطريق الفداء عن نفسه إذ الله تعالى على كل أحد من خلقه نعمة الإيجاد فشكره يكون بإعدام نفسه طلبا لمرضاته، كما كان شكر نعمة المال بإزالة بعضه عن نفسه، شكر نعمة المنكح والمأكل والمشرب الامتناع عنها بالصوم، إلا أن كل واحد منهم، لو أتلف نفسه شكرا لنعمة الوجود، لانقطع النسل والبشر، وتفانى الخلق وارتفع الجنس المقصود من الخلائق، فاكتفى الصانع بكمال حكمته بفدية يفديها عن نفسه، كما في حق الذبيح عليه السلام. ثم هذا كله منا تبرع، إذ لا حاجة بنا إلى بيان شيء من هذا.
Then offering sacrifices (qurban) is all by way of ransom (fida') for oneself, since Allah Almighty has bestowed upon every one of His creatures the grace of existence. So gratitude for it would be by annihilating oneself seeking His pleasure, just as gratitude for the blessing of wealth is by removing some of it from oneself, and gratitude for the blessing of marriage, food, and drink is by abstaining from them through fasting. However, if each of them were to destroy himself as gratitude for the blessing of existence, then progeny and humanity would be cut off, the creatures would perish, and the intended genus would cease from creation. So the Maker, by His perfect wisdom, sufficed with a ransom that one gives on behalf of oneself, as in the case of the sacrificed one (al-dhabih), peace be upon him. Then all this from us is gratuitous, for we have no need to explain any of this.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the rationale behind animal sacrifice (qurban). The author argues that the greatest blessing from God is existence itself, and the proper gratitude would be to sacrifice one's own life. However, if everyone did that, the human race would end. Therefore, God in His wisdom instituted animal sacrifice as a proxy (fida') for the self, exemplified by the story of the 'dhabih' (Ishmael) who was ransomed with a ram. The author concludes that this whole argument is gratuitous on his part, as there is no need for such detailed explanation.

Correction: The passage frames sacrifice as a proxy for self-sacrifice in gratitude for existence, not as atonement.

Key Takeaway

?
The author says this explanation is gratuitous; the command itself is enough. Are you willing to obey Allah's commands even when you do not fully grasp the wisdom behind them? What does your response to this passage reveal about your trust in His perfect wisdom?

Explaining the Hadith of Adam's Creation in God's Image
Al-Nasafi explains the hadith by clarifying the pronoun reference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two possible interpretations of the pronoun in the hadith 'God created Adam in His image' and why these interpretations protect divine transcendence.

Core Idea
The pronoun in the hadith refers to a human, not to God.

One of the most frequently misunderstood hadiths is the Prophet's statement that God created Adam in His image. Some have mistakenly thought this implies God has a physical form. In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi clarifies the occasion of the hadith and offers two plausible interpretations that keep God's transcendence intact. Let's read his explanation directly.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it too deeply. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall meaning. Let the author's own words set the context.
Pay attention to the structure: occasion, two interpretations, benefit.
2
Identify the two pronoun referents
The author gives two possibilities for the pronoun 'his' in 'his image.' First, it refers to the man being struck. Second, it could refer to Adam himself. Identify these in the text.
The first interpretation is the primary explanation linked to the occasion.
3
Understand the occasion and its significance
The hadith was said in response to a man striking another on the face. The Prophet forbade striking faces and linked it to the hadith. Understand how the occasion shapes the meaning.
This context helps avoid anthropomorphism.
4
Reflect on the theological benefit
Both interpretations remove any implication that God has a physical form. The benefit is preserving the doctrine of divine transcendence (tanzih). Think about why this is important in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما المروي أنه تعالى خلق آدم على صورته فهو خارج على سبب يروى، وهو أنه صلى الله عليه رأى رجلا يضرب آخر على وجهه فنهاه عن الضرب على الوجه وقال: 'إن الله تعالى خلق آدم على صورته' أي صورة المضروب فكانت الهاء راجعة إلى المضروب لا إلى الله تعالى، ويحتمل أن تكون الهاء راجعة إلى آدم عليه السلام، وفائدة الحديث أن الله خلق آدم على صورته التي شوهد عليها الدنيا لم تغير صورته عند إخراجه من الجنة إلى الدنيا كما غيرت صورة
As for the narration that He, exalted, created Adam in His image, it is based on a transmitted occasion: that he (peace be upon him) saw a man striking another on his face and forbade striking on the face and said: 'Indeed Allah created Adam in his image' – meaning the image of the one struck, so the pronoun refers to the one struck, not to Allah. And it is possible that the pronoun refers to Adam, peace be upon him. The benefit of the hadith is that Allah created Adam in his image which he was seen upon in the world; his form was not changed when he was taken out of Paradise to the world, unlike the forms of others.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage provides an interpretation of the well-known hadith 'God created Adam in His image.' The author first gives the occasion for the hadith: the Prophet saw a man striking another on the face and forbade it, and then said this statement. The pronoun 'his' (الهاء) can be understood in two ways. First, it refers to the man who was struck ('image of the struck one'), meaning Adam was created in the likeness of that person, not God. Second, it could refer to Adam himself, meaning Adam was created in his own image (the form he had in Paradise), and that form did not change when he was sent down to earth, unlike the forms of other beings that changed. In either case, the hadith does not imply that God has a physical image. This is a classic example of ta'wil (allegorical interpretation) to avoid anthropomorphism and maintain divine transcendence.

Key Terms
صورة آدم
الهاء
التأويل
الضرب على الوجه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith proves that God has a physical form or image.
Correction: The author shows that the pronoun 'his' refers to a human (the struck person or Adam), not to God, so the hadith does not attribute a physical image to God.

Checkpoint
In the hadith 'God created Adam in His image,' to whom does the pronoun 'His' primarily refer according to the first explanation given in the passage?
A) God
B) The person being struck
C) Adam
D) The Prophet

Key Takeaway
The hadith's pronoun refers to a human (the struck person or Adam), not to God, preserving divine transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This hadith forbids striking the face because humans are created with dignity. In what ways do you dishonor others, perhaps through words or neglect, that you need to repent from?
?
Al-Nasafi offers two interpretations, both avoiding anthropomorphism. When you encounter ambiguous texts, do you rush to a literal meaning that might contradict core beliefs about God? How can you train yourself to seek sound interpretations?
