Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that foolishness depends on a prohibition; what is foolish for creatures is not automatically foolish for the Creator.

?

God's Power to Distinguish Prophet from False Prophet
Nasafi defends God's ability to differentiate between true and false prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that God's perfect power necessarily includes the ability to distinguish true prophets from false ones.

Core Idea
God's perfect power leaves no room for incapacity in distinguishing truth from falsehood.

Al-Nasafi here confronts a theological objection: if false prophets can imitate miracles, how can we know which prophet is true? Some groups argued that God cannot distinguish between them. Nasafi responds that this objection implies a limitation on God's power, which contradicts the established truth that God is perfect in power and incapable of weakness. In this short but dense passage, he defends God's absolute ability to differentiate, grounding it in divine perfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Carefully read the Arabic text and its English translation. Pay attention to the objection (what 'the other group' claims) and Nasafi's rebuttal.
The passage is only a few lines but contains a complete argument.
2
Identify the objection and its implication
What reasons do the objectors give for why God cannot distinguish? What consequence does Nasafi draw from their claim?
The objectors mention changing natures and counterfeiting.
3
Analyze the refutation
Note how Nasafi uses the established attribute of perfect power to counter the objection. Why does he say God must be capable of distinguishing?
Think about the concepts of 'kāmil al-qudra' and 'nafādh al-mashī'a'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما تعلق به الفرق الآخر من امتناع التفرقة بين النبي والمتنبئ لامتناع تغيير الطباع، أو لإمكان المعارضة وغير ذلك، كل ذلك موجب عجز الباري جل وعلا عن التفرقة بين الصادق والكاذب، وقد ثبت بالدلائل الواضحة أن صانع العالم جل وعلا كامل القدرة يستحيل عليه العجز فكان قادرًا على ذلك ضرورة كمال قدرته ونفاذ مشيئته.
And what the other group clung to – the impossibility of distinguishing between the prophet and the false prophet due to the impossibility of changing natures, or the possibility of counterfeiting, and other such things – all of that implies that the Creator, Exalted and Majestic, is incapable of distinguishing between the truthful and the liar. Yet it has been established by clear proofs that the Maker of the world, Exalted and Majestic, is perfect in power; incapacity is impossible for Him. He is powerful over that necessarily, due to the perfection of His power and the effectiveness of His will.
Source pages p. 675

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection raised by a group (likely the Barāhima or skeptics) who argue that God cannot distinguish between a true prophet and a false claimant. They base this on the impossibility of changing human natures (so a false prophet could imitate miracles) or the possibility of counterfeiting. Al-Nasafi responds that accepting this would imply that God is incapable of distinguishing truth from falsehood, which contradicts His perfect power. Since we have clear proofs that God is perfect in power (kāmil al-qudra) and incapacity (ʿajz) is impossible for Him, He must be able to make such a distinction. This follows necessarily from His perfect power and the effectiveness (nafādh) of His will. The argument is that any supposed hindrance is irrelevant because God's power is absolute.

Key Terms
تفرقة
نبي
متنبئ
عجز
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The existence of false prophets or the possibility of counterfeiting shows that God cannot distinguish between true and false prophets.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues that any such impossibility would imply God's incapacity, but God's perfect power means He is necessarily able to distinguish.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence that al-Nasafi draws from the claim that God cannot distinguish between a prophet and a false prophet?
A) That God is just in sending prophets
B) That God would be incapable, which is impossible
C) That prophethood is unnecessary
D) That miracles are not needed

Key Takeaway
Nasafi establishes that God's perfect power necessarily includes the ability to distinguish truthful prophets from false claimants, contrary to objections based on changing natures or counterfeiting.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter confusion or conflicting claims about truth in your life—whether in matters of faith, relationships, or decisions—do you sincerely rely on God's perfect ability to make the truth clear to you, or do you depend primarily on your own reasoning? What would change if you truly believed that God's power is fully capable of distinguishing truth from falsehood for you?
?
The opposing group argued that God cannot distinguish because natures are fixed. Where in your own heart have you assumed that God's power is limited by your circumstances, habits, or the 'way things are'? Name one area where you have implicitly placed a limit on God's ability to intervene, and commit to praying about it this week.
?
Nasafi teaches that God's power necessitates His ability to distinguish between the truthful and the liar. How does this truth challenge you to live with greater integrity, knowing that God can and will expose falsehood—both in the world and in your own heart? What step will you take today to align your actions with the truth that God sees and distinguishes all?

The Rational Status of Prophethood: Possible or Necessary?
Nasafi presents and explains the two positions on whether prophethood is rationally possible or necessary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two positions on whether prophethood is rationally possible or obligatory, and the precise meaning of 'wājib' in this debate.

Core Idea
Prophethood is either rationally possible or necessary — but 'necessary' means certain, not imposed.

Al-Nasafi presents a key disagreement among theologians: is prophethood something God may or may not do, or is it a necessary consequence of His wisdom? Understanding this debate requires careful attention to how each side uses terms like 'possible' and 'obligatory'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
Read the passage and note the two positions: some say prophethood is among the possible things; others say it is obligatory. Who holds each view?
The first group is the majority of the People of Hadith; the second includes those who affirm rational obligation of gratitude.
2
Clarify the meaning of 'wājib'
Al-Nasafi explains that 'wājib' here does not mean an external obligation on God. Instead, it means extreme certainty of existence. Compare with 'impossible' as extreme certainty of non-existence.
The word 'wujūb' is used for certainty, not moral obligation.
3
Understand the reasoning
The second group argues that prophethood is required by God's wisdom; its non-existence would be foolishness. Reflect on the analogy with God's knowledge: what He knows will exist must exist.
This shows how rational obligation is tied to divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن متكلمي أهل الإسلام اختلفوا فيما بينهم أن الرسالة من قبل الممكنات في العقل، أم هي من جملة الواجبات؟ فذهب جميع متكلمي أهل الحديث سوى أبي العباس القلانسي إلى أنها من جملة الممكنات، وذهب القائلون بأن العقل آلة معرفة الحسن والقبيح ووجوب شكر المنعم إلى القول بوجوبها، ولا يعنون بكونها واجبة أنها وجبت على الله بإيجاب أحد أو بإيجابه على نفسه بل يريدون أنها متحققة الوجود، ويقولون: إن الوجوب الحقيقة لفظة بها عن فضل تأكد لوجود المذكور، كما أن الامتناع لفظة يعبر بها عن تأكد لا وجوده، وهما في الحقيقة متقابلان تقابل الأضداد، وإنما يقولون: إنها متأكدة الوجود لأنها من مقتضيات حكمة القديم جل وعلا، ويستحيل أن لا يوجد ما كان وجوده من مقتضيات حكمته لما أن انعدامه يكون من باب السفه وهو يستحيل على القديم عز وجل، هذا كما أن ما علم الله وجوده يتحقق وجوده لا محالة ويكون واجب الوجود أي متأكد الوجود، لا أن وجوبه بإيجاب أحد على الله تعالى بل لأن وجوده يتحقق لا محالة لما أن انعدامه يوجب الجهل به، وهو مما يستحيل على القديم عز وجل وإلى هذا القول ذهب جميع من يقول بوجوب شكر المنعم.
Then the theologians of the people of Islam disagreed among themselves: is prophethood among the intellectually possible things (al-mumkināt) or is it among the obligatory things (al-wājibāt)? All the theologians of the People of Hadith except Abū al-ʿAbbās al-Qalānisī held that it is among the possible things. Those who held that reason is an instrument for knowing good and evil and the obligation to thank the Benefactor held that it is obligatory. They do not mean by its being obligatory that it is incumbent upon God due to someone else's imposition or His own imposition upon Himself; rather they mean that it is necessarily realized in existence (mutaḥaqqiqat al-wujūd). They say that the word 'obligatory' (wujūb) in reality is an expression for the extreme certainty of the existence of the mentioned thing, just as 'impossibility' (imtināʿ) is an expression for the extreme certainty of its non-existence. They are in reality opposites, like the opposition of contraries. They only say that it is certain of existence because it is among the requirements of the wisdom of the Eternal, Exalted and Majestic. It is impossible that what is required by His wisdom should not exist, because its non-existence would be from the category of foolishness (safah), which is impossible for the Eternal, Exalted and Majestic. This is like what God knows will exist – its existence is necessarily realized and it is wājib al-wujūd (necessary of existence), i.e., certain of existence, not because its obligation is due to someone imposing on God, but because its existence is necessarily realized because its non-existence would entail ignorance of it, which is impossible for the Eternal, Exalted and Majestic. And to this view went all those who affirm the obligation to thank the Benefactor.
Source pages p. 676

Commentary
This passage presents the disagreement among Islamic theologians regarding the rational status of prophethood. Some, including the majority of the People of Hadith (except al-Qalānisī), hold that prophethood is rationally possible (mumkin) – i.e., it is among the contingent things that God may or may not do. Others, namely those who affirm that reason can independently know good and evil and that gratitude to the Benefactor is rationally obligatory (wājib shukr al-munʿim), hold that prophethood is obligatory (wājib). The author clarifies that these theologians do not mean obligatory in the sense of an obligation imposed upon God by another or by Himself. Rather, they mean that prophethood is necessarily realized in existence (mutaḥaqqiqat al-wujūd). They use 'wujūb' to express extreme certainty of existence, similar to how 'imtināʿ' expresses extreme certainty of non-existence. The two are opposite concepts. They argue that prophethood is certain of existence because it is a requirement of God's eternal wisdom. It is impossible for something required by His wisdom not to exist, since its absence would be foolishness (safah), which is impossible for God. The author then draws an analogy: just as what God knows will exist must necessarily exist (and is called wājib al-wujūd, not due to any imposition, but because its non-existence would imply ignorance in God), so too prophethood is certain. This view is adopted by all who affirm the rational obligation of gratitude to the Benefactor (i.e., the Muʿtazila).

Key Terms
رسالة
ممكنات
واجبات
حكمة
سفه
شكر المنعم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'wājib' in this context means God is obligated by an external command or by His own command.
Correction: Al-Nasafi explains that 'wājib' here means extreme certainty of existence, not a moral or legal obligation. It is used to indicate that something must exist because it is required by God's wisdom.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do those who affirm the rational obligation of prophethood mean by 'wājib'?
A) That prophethood is imposed on God by another
B) That God is obliged by His own command
C) That prophethood is certain to exist due to God's wisdom
D) That prophethood is impossible not to exist due to human need

Key Takeaway
The debate over prophethood's rational status hinges on what 'wājib' means — for some, it indicates certainty from wisdom, not imposed obligation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider God's wisdom in sending prophets, is your belief in prophethood merely a possibility you accept, or is it a certainty that shapes how you live today? Are you living as if prophethood were a necessary reality from God's wisdom, or just a historical possibility?
?
If you truly believed that non-existence of prophethood would imply foolishness in God, would you treat the Prophet's guidance with the same weight as the fact that the sun rises? What would change in your daily reliance on his teachings?
?
You affirm that gratitude to the Benefactor (shukr al-munʿim) is obligatory—but are you actually grateful? How would your life look different if you acted on the certainty that God's wisdom required sending a messenger to guide you?

The Premise All Sides Accept: Reason Knows Good and Evil
Nasafi frames the dialectical approach against deniers of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi uses the deniers' own admission of reason's role to build a common ground for arguing for prophethood.

Core Idea
Deniers of prophethood already rely on reason, so they concede its moral knowledge.

When arguing with those who deny prophethood, we cannot assume revelation. But we can turn their own method against them: they use reason to reject prophethood, so they must admit that reason can discern good from evil. Imam Nasafi capitalizes on this agreement, sparing us the task of proving reason's capability from scratch.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic original once, then the translation. Notice how the author states he has already proven that reason can know good/evil elsewhere, but here he takes a different route.
The passage has density; read slowly.
2
Identify the two approaches
The author contrasts two methods: proving reason's ability directly, and building on the denier's own admission. Locate where he says he will not repeat the proof.
3
Understand the denier's dilemma
The author points out that deniers use reason to deny prophethood. How does that force them to agree that reason can know good/evil? Ponder the logic.
Revelation is not an option for them, so reason is their only tool.
4
Appreciate the strategic move
Instead of arguing from first principles, Nasafi builds on agreed premises. This is a classic dialectical method in kalam.
It makes the argument efficient and harder for the opponent to reject.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قبل ورود الشرع، وبالوقوف على الحسن والقبيح بمجرد العقول. ولا معنى للاشتغال ببيان دلائل هذه المسألة وإني قد بينت ذلك على استقصاء في تصنيف (۱) لي (۲) في تلك المسألة، وإنما الحاجة هاهنا إلى بيان القول بوجوبها على منكريها، ولا شك أن من أنكر الرسالة وعدها في حيز الممتنعات فعل ذلك بالعقل دون السمع، إذ السمع بلا ثبوت الرسالة محال، فثبت من نفاة(٣) الرسالة المساعدة على القول بأن العقل مما يوقف به على الحكمة والسفه والواجب والممتنع والحسن والقبيح. فنتكلم معهم على هذه الطريقة بناء للأمر على مساعدتهم دون (٤) الاشتغال بإثبات معرفة ذلك بمجرد العقول بالدليل فنقول وبالله التوفيق
Before the advent of revelation, and by means of reason alone, [one can] know good and evil. There is no point in busying oneself with explaining the proofs of this matter, and I have indeed explained it exhaustively in a work (1) of mine (2) on that matter. Rather, the need here is to state the opinion of its obligation upon its deniers. There is no doubt that whoever denies prophethood and considers it among the impossibilities does so by reason, not by revelation, since revelation without establishing prophethood is impossible. So it is established from the deniers (3) of prophethood the agreement that reason is that by which one can know wisdom and foolishness, the obligatory and the impossible, good and evil. So we speak with them in this manner, building the matter on their agreement, without (4) busying ourselves with proving the knowledge of that by means of reason alone through evidence. We say, and with God is success.
Source pages p. 677

Commentary
This passage establishes a common ground with those who deny prophethood. The author states that there is no need to prove that reason can know good and evil before revelation, as he has already done so elsewhere. Instead, he will argue directly with deniers based on their own admission. He points out that even those who deny prophethood do so by using reason, not revelation, because revelation cannot be accepted without first establishing prophethood. Therefore, they must admit that reason can discern wisdom from foolishness, the obligatory from the impossible, and good from evil. Thus, the author will build his argument on this agreed premise, sparing the burden of proving reason's capability from scratch.

Key Terms

الحسن والقبيح
الرسالة
السمع
الممتنع
الواجب
الحكمة والسفه
نفاة الرسالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author is trying to prove that reason is sufficient for all religious knowledge.
Correction: Nasafi is only establishing a premise that his opponents already accept; he is not arguing for reason's sufficiency in every matter.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the author not need to prove that reason can know good and evil?
A) Because it is self-evident
B) Because he has already done so in another work
C) Because revelation proves it
D) Because the deniers reject it

Key Takeaway
Nasafi's argumentative strategy is to ground the discussion on a premise that even the denier of prophethood must accept: reason's ability to discern good and evil.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you debate with someone who rejects a core Islamic belief, do you first pause to identify what you both already accept? Or do you rush to defend your position? What would change if you deliberately started from common ground, as Nasafi did?
?
Think of a specific person you know who denies or doubts prophethood or any aspect of revelation. What rational premise do you share with them that could serve as a starting point for dialogue? Are you willing to set aside proving reason's capability and instead build on their own use of reason?
?
Nasafi chose not to re-prove the rational basis for good and evil, but instead used the opponent's own method. Is there an area in your life where you insist on proving something from scratch rather than acknowledging what the other person already concedes? How might that change your approach?

Reason's Inability to Distinguish Harmful Substances
Nasafi argues that reason cannot distinguish harmful substances, necessitating prophecy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why reason and senses are insufficient to distinguish beneficial from harmful substances, and how this necessitates prophetic guidance.

Core Idea
Reason cannot safely test substances; divine revelation is essential for survival.

Imam Nasafi presents a powerful argument from human experience: we rely on food and medicine to live, but many substances that look similar are deadly poisons. Our senses and reason cannot tell them apart without risk. This passage shows that without divine guidance, the very creation of these substances would be futile, implying that God must have sent prophets to clarify what is beneficial and harmful.

Guided Path
1
Identify the foundational premises
Read the opening lines where Nasafi states that God created humans with a need for food and a desire for survival, and that He created both nourishments and deadly poisons from the same kinds of substances.
Notice the emphasis on 'according to custom' (على ما عليه العادة) – this is a key concept in Maturidi thought.
2
Understand the limitation of reason and senses
Nasafi argues that neither senses nor reason can distinguish between the beneficial and harmful substances. Experimentation is too risky because immediate effects may not appear, and delayed effects could be fatal.
Consider the example: some poisons show harm only after a week, a month, or a year.
3
Follow the dilemma of a person trying to survive
Nasafi presents a scenario: if someone orders another to eat an unknown substance to see if it's safe, they risk that person's life. If they wait to observe long-term effects, they starve. This illustrates the impossibility of relying on trial and error.
This dilemma shows that without prior knowledge, survival is impossible.
4
Grasp the first aspect (وجه) of the argument
After the detailed scenario, Nasafi states the first of several arguments: if God had not clarified the distinction, and if rational people had not dared to experiment, then the creation of nourishments would lack wisdom and imply futility – which cannot be attributed to God.
This directly leads to the necessity of divine guidance (prophethood).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن من المعلوم الذي لا خفاء به على من اعترف بالصانع أن الصانع جل جلالة خلق الخلق ولم يجعل على ما عليه العادة بقاءهم إلا بالأغذية وحبب إليهم البقاء، وجعل في جنس ما خلق ما بالخلق إليه بطباعهم رغبة لما فيه من اللذة والشهوة، ثم إنه تعالى كما خلق ما لهم به البقاء من الأغذية، وما يحفظ عليهم الصحة التامة ويزيل عنهم العلل العارضة من الأدوية، خلق من جنس تلك الجواهر السموم القاتلة والجواهر المتلفة، وليس في قوة الحواس ولا في جبلة العقل الوقوف على ما يمتاز به البعض عن البعض ولا الاطلاع على ما يوجب التفرقة بين كل من ذلك، ولا يطبق العقل التجربة بنفسه لما فيه من خطر الهلاك ولا بمن تحت يديه لما فيه من تعريض الغير على التو (۱) أو التلف، مع أن ما هو المقصود من الوقوف على ذلك لا يحصل إلا بالتجربة إذ ليس كل سم يقتل من ساعته، ولا كل مضر يظهر أثره عقيب تناوله، إذ من السموم ما يظهر أثره ويتفاقم ضرره بعد أسبوع، ومنه ما يظهر ذلك بعد شهر وبعد سنة، معروف ذلك عند المختصين بعلم جواهر الأشياء وطبائع الموجودات، ولو أمر غيره ممن تحت تصرفه بتناول (ذلك يتناول) (۳) هو بنفسه ذلك ليدفع به عن (٤) نفسه ألم الجوع وضرر العطش ويحصل له به ما هو محبوبة من البقاء إذ لم ير أثر ضرر ظهر عن تناوله لأدى ذلك عسى إلى تلف مهجته وفساد بنيته بعد ذلك بزمان لما كان ذلك المتناول مما يضر بعد شهر أو سنة، ولو أمسك عن تناول الأغذية منتظرا ظهور (٥) أثره (٦) إلى شهر أو سنة لمات جوعًا وعطشاً قبل بلوغ ما ينتظره من المدة. (۲) ثم بعد هذا نقرر الكلام من وجوه أحدها أن الصانع جل (۷) وعلا لو لم يبين الأغذية من الأدوية والسموم، ولم يتجاسر العقلاء على التجربة، ولم يتوصلوا إلى الانتفاع بالأغذية، واستدامة مهجتهم، لم يكن لخلق الأغذية التي هي ما عليه العادة الجارية أسباب البقاء حكمة ويحصل إيجادها على العبث والسفه جل الله عن ذلك.
Indeed, among the known matters which are not hidden to anyone who acknowledges the Maker is that the Maker—exalted is His majesty—created creation and did not make their survival, according to custom, except through nourishments, and He instilled in them love for survival, and He placed in the kind of what He created that which the creation has by their nature a desire for, due to the pleasure and appetite in it. Then, just as He created the nourishments by which they survive, and the medicines which preserve their complete health and remove from them accidental ailments, He created from the same kind of substances the deadly poisons and destructive substances. Neither in the power of the senses nor in the innate disposition of reason is there the ability to know what distinguishes some from others, nor to know what necessitates differentiation between all of that. Reason cannot apply experiment by itself due to the risk of destruction, nor can it [apply experiment] through those under its authority due to the exposure of others to destruction (1) or loss. Moreover, the intended purpose of knowing that is not attained except through experiment, since not every poison kills instantly, nor does every harmful thing show its effect immediately after consumption. Among poisons are those whose effect appears and whose harm intensifies after a week, and among them are those whose effect appears after a month and after a year—that is known among specialists in the science of the substances and natures of existing things. If he were to order someone else under his authority to consume that [which he would himself consume] (3) to ward off the pain of hunger and the harm of thirst and to obtain for himself what is beloved of survival—since he sees no harmful effect from consuming it—that could lead to the destruction of his life and corruption of his constitution after a time, because that consumed thing harms after a month or a year. And if he were to refrain from consuming nourishments, waiting for its effect (5) to appear (6) for a month or a year, he would die of hunger and thirst before reaching the time he awaits. (2) Then after this, we present the speech from aspects: one of them is that if the Maker—mighty (7) and exalted—had not clarified the nourishments from the medicines and poisons, and the rational people had not dared to experiment, and they had not arrived at benefiting from nourishments and perpetuating their lives, then there would be no wisdom in creating the nourishments which are, according to custom, the means of survival, and their creation would be futile and foolish—exalted is God above that.
Source pages p. 677

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed argument for the necessity of divine guidance (prophethood). The author begins with a premise acknowledged by anyone who believes in God: that God created humans with a need for food and a love for survival. He also created both beneficial things (foods, medicines) and harmful things (poisons, destructive substances). However, human senses and reason alone cannot distinguish between them. Experiment is risky because immediate trial may lead to death, and delaying consumption to observe long-term effects results in starvation. Even experts rely on experience. The author illustrates with a scenario: a person cannot safely test unknown substances by ordering another to eat them, nor can he wait indefinitely to see effects. Therefore, since God's creation of these substances would be futile if humans could not benefit from the good and avoid the harmful, a divine clarification (i.e., revelation through prophets) is necessary. The first aspect (وجه) of the argument is then presented: if God had not distinguished these substances and if humans had not dared to experiment, the creation of nourishments as means of survival would lack wisdom, implying foolishness – which is an absurd attribution to God. Thus, prophecy is required to guide humans to what benefits them and away from what harms them.

Key Terms
الصانع
الأغذية
السموم
الأدوية
الحواس
العقل
التجربة
الحكمة
العبث والسفه
البعثة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument proves that reason is completely useless and unreliable.
Correction: The argument does not deny reason's value in other domains; it only shows its limitation in occult matters where empirical testing is risky or impossible, necessitating divine revelation.

Checkpoint
What is the first aspect (وجه) of the argument presented after the discussion of food and poison?
A) That humans need food to survive
B) That without divine clarification, the creation of nourishments would lack wisdom
C) That experiment is too risky
D) That reason is completely useless

Key Takeaway
Reason and senses alone cannot distinguish beneficial from harmful substances, so divine guidance through prophets is necessary for human survival and to avoid divine futility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This argument shows that without God’s guidance, you would not even be able to eat safely. In what areas of your life are you still trusting your own judgment over the clear guidance of the Qur’an and Sunnah? What specific change can you make today to submit to that guidance?
?
The passage says God 'instilled in them love for survival.' That survival instinct is a gift, yet you often act as if you are self-sufficient. Where has your self-reliance led you into spiritual or moral harm? Will you admit your dependence on God’s prophets for direction?
?
If God had not clarified, creation would be futile. When you ignore or neglect the prophetic guidance, do you not make your own life feel futile—chasing what seems good but leads to harm? What is one thing you will commit to learning from the prophetic example this week to restore meaning to your life?

The Dilemma of Distinguishing Foods from Poisons
Demonstrates necessity of divine guidance due to fallibility of human experimentation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why human reason and experimentation cannot reliably distinguish beneficial foods from harmful poisons, and why this establishes the need for divine guidance.

Core Idea
Only divine guidance can solve the dilemma of delayed poisons versus immediate need.

Imām al-Nasafī presents a compelling argument that human reason, even with experimentation, cannot reliably tell foods from poisons. The reason is not just the risk of immediate death, but the deceptive nature of delayed poisons. This creates a practical dilemma that only divine revelation can resolve. As you read the passage, notice how he sets up the problem step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument in Arabic and English
First, read the Arabic passage aloud or silently. Then read the English translation to get the full meaning. Pay attention to the flow of the argument.
The passage uses technical terms like 'تجربة' (experiment) and 'مهجة' (life).
2
Identify the core problem
Find the two main obstacles the author presents: the risk of direct harm from experiment, and the inability to delegate the risk to others. Then note the key fact: many poisons have delayed effects.
3
Walk through the dilemma
The author illustrates a hypothetical scenario. Outline the two options: either order someone else to taste and you eat, or refrain from eating to observe effects. What are the consequences of each?
This shows the impossibility of rational determination.
4
Understand the conclusion
The argument implies that only a divine lawgiver could clearly mark what is safe. This prepares the ground for proving the necessity of prophethood.
This connects to the broader theme of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على ما يمتاز به البعض عن البعض ولا الاطلاع على ما يوجب التفرقة بين كل من ذلك، ولا يطبق العقل التجربة بنفسه لما فيه من خطر الهلاك ولا بمن تحت يديه لما فيه من تعريض الغير على التلف، مع أن ما هو المقصود من الوقوف على ذلك لا يحصل إلا بالتجربة إذ ليس كل سم يقتل من ساعته، ولا كل مضر يظهر أثره عقيب تناوله، إذ من السموم ما يظهر أثره ويتفاقم ضرره بعد أسبوع، ومنه ما يظهر ذلك بعد شهر وبعد سنة، معروف ذلك عند المختصين بعلم جواهر الأشياء وطبائع الموجودات، ولو أمر غيره ممن تحت تصرفه بتناول ذلك يتناول هو بنفسه ذلك ليدفع به عن نفسه ألم الجوع وضرر العطش ويحصل له به ما هو محبوبة من البقاء إذ لم ير أثر ضرر ظهر عن تناوله لأدى ذلك عسى إلى تلف مهجته وفساد بنيته بعد ذلك بزمان لما كان ذلك المتناول مما يضر بعد شهر أو سنة، ولو أمسك عن تناول الأغذية منتظرا ظهور أثره إلى شهر أو سنة لمات جوعاً وعطشاً قبل بلوغ ما ينتظره من المدة.
On that by which some things are distinguished from others, and lack of knowledge of what necessitates differentiation between each of that, and the intellect does not apply experiment by itself due to the risk of destruction, nor by those under his authority due to exposing others to destruction, while that which is intended of knowing that is not obtained except through experiment, since not every poison kills instantly, nor does every harmful thing show its effect immediately after consumption, for among poisons are those whose effect appears and its harm worsens after a week, and among them are those whose effect appears after a month and after a year, known among specialists in the science of the essences of things and the natures of existents. And if he commands someone else under his authority to consume that, he himself consumes that to ward off from himself the pain of hunger and harm of thirst and obtain that which is beloved of survival, since he did not see the effect of harm appearing from its consumption, that would perhaps lead to the destruction of his life and corruption of his constitution after that time, since that consumer is something harmful after a month or a year. And if he refrained from consuming foods, waiting for its effect to appear in a month or a year, he would die of hunger and thirst before reaching the period he awaits.
Source pages p. 678

Commentary
This passage is a preliminary argument establishing the impossibility of humans distinguishing beneficial from harmful substances through reason or experiment alone. The author begins by noting that the intellect cannot safely apply experiment due to the risk of destruction, nor can it delegate to others due to exposing them to harm. Then he explains that the delayed effects of poisons (some appearing after a week, month, or year) make it impossible to rely on immediate observation. He illustrates the dilemma: if a person orders someone else to taste a substance while he himself consumes it to satisfy hunger, he risks delayed harm; if he refrains from eating while waiting to see if harm occurs, he dies of hunger in the meantime. This demonstrates the need for divine guidance to clearly distinguish foods from poisons.

Key Terms
تجربة
سم
مضر
مهجة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That human experimentation is sufficient to determine what is beneficial and harmful.
Correction: The passage shows that delayed effects make experimentation unreliable, and the practical dilemma of needing to eat while unsure of safety proves that reason alone cannot suffice.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is experiment alone insufficient for distinguishing foods from poisons?
A) Poisons always kill instantly, so experiment is too risky.
B) Many poisons have delayed effects, so one cannot observe immediate results.
C) The intellect is too weak to perform experiments.
D) Humans do not have the authority to experiment on others.

Key Takeaway
Human reason cannot resolve the conflicting needs of immediate survival and delayed harm; this shows the need for divine guidance.

?
This lesson shows that human experimentation is insufficient for distinguishing food from poison. Where else do you trust your own experience over revelation? What step will you take to submit to divine guidance this week?

First Proof: Without Divine Specification, Creation Would Be Futile
A conditional argument for divine specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first proof for the necessity of divine guidance: that without it, creation would be futile.

Core Idea
Without God's guidance, creation would be meaningless — an act of futility.

This lesson presents the first formal proof from the text. The author argues that if God had not distinguished foods from poisons, rational people could not safely benefit from them, and the creation of foods — intended for survival — would be pointless. Such futility is impossible for Allah, so divine specification through revelation is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the conditional structure: 'if not... then...'
The key terms are صانع, عبث, سفه, حكمة.
2
Identify the argument's structure
Notice that the argument uses a counterfactual: if God had not distinguished foods from medicines and poisons, then creation would be futile. This proves that God must have provided such distinction.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: why does this proof demonstrate the need for prophecy? The answer: because without revelation, humans cannot know which foods are safe, making creation pointless.
This connects to the broader theme of prophethood.

Source Text

Then after this we present the discussion in aspects: one of them is that the Maker, may He be glorified and exalted, if He had not distinguished the foods from the medicines and poisons, and the rational people did not dare to experiment, and they did not reach benefiting from foods and the continuation of their lives, then the creation of foods, which are according to the customary course the means of survival, would not be wisdom, and their existence would occur in vain and foolishness—exalted is Allah above that.
Source pages p. 678

Commentary
This passage presents the first formal proof for the necessity of divine specification. The author states that if God had not distinguished foods from medicines and poisons, and if rational people could not safely experiment to benefit from foods for survival, then the creation of foods—which are normally the means of survival—would not be wisdom (hikma). Instead, their existence would be characterized by 'abath (futility) and safah (foolishness), which are impossible for God, who is exalted above such. Thus, God must have provided a clear distinction through revelation.

Second Proof: Annihilation Without Means Would Be Purposeful
Second proof for necessity of prophethood via purpose of creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second proof that without divine guidance, creation would be purposeless annihilation, necessitating prophetic revelation.

Core Idea
Creation cannot exist solely for annihilation; wisdom demands divine guidance.

This passage presents a rational argument for the necessity of prophethood. If bodies were not given access to means of survival such as food, they would perish in the shortest time, with no purpose beyond annihilation. Such a creation would be considered ugly by reason and outside wisdom. Therefore, there must be a divine statement from the Creator, conveyed through chosen servants, to render creation wise and meaningful.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic original and the translation carefully. Notice the conditional structure: 'if...then...'.
The author uses a hypothetical scenario to prove the need for revelation.
2
Identify the logical chain
Trace the argument: (1) Without survival means, bodies perish quickly. (2) That would make creation only for annihilation. (3) Such a purpose is rationally ugly. (4) Hence, divine guidance is required to avoid foolishness.
3
Connect to the need for prophets
Understand that the 'bayan' (statement) from the Creator comes through prophets. This proof shows that prophethood is not arbitrary but rationally necessary for wisdom in creation.
This argument complements the first proof (not included here).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني: أن أبدان الممتحنين لو لم يجعل لهم الوصول إلى ما هو من أسباب بقائها تلفت بأوهى مدة وأسرع زمان من غير حصول معنى لإيجادهم سوى الفناء، وخلق الخلق للفناء خاصة من غير عاقبة حميدة تتعلق به مستقبح في العقول خارج عن الحكمة فلا بد من البيان الوارد من منشئ الأشياء على طبائعها المختلفة، العالم بجواهرها وما يتعلق بها من الحكمة على لسان ما شاء من عباده، ليخرج تخليق الجواهر التي هي من أسباب البقاء وأحداث الأبدان المحتاجة في دوامها وبقائها إلى الأغذية المجعولة أسبابًا لذلك عن السفه ويدخل في حيز ما هو حكمة.
And the second: that the bodies of the tested ones, if they are not given access to that which is from the means of their survival, they would perish in the weakest period and fastest time without obtaining any meaning for their existence except annihilation, and creating creation only for annihilation without a praiseworthy consequence attached to it is considered ugly in the intellects, outside wisdom. So there must be a statement coming from the Originator of things upon their different natures, the Knower of their essences and the wisdom related to them, upon the tongue of whomever He wills from His servants, so that the creation of the essences that are means of survival and the generation of bodies that are in need in their continuity and survival of foods made as means for that may exit from foolishness and enter into the realm of wisdom.
Source pages p. 679

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof: if bodies were not given access to means of survival (foods), they would quickly perish in the weakest and fastest time, with no purpose other than annihilation (fana'). Creating beings solely for annihilation, without a praiseworthy consequence, is considered ugly (mustaqbah) in the intellects and outside wisdom. Therefore, there must be a divine statement (bayan) from the Creator, who knows the essences and wisdom of things, communicated through the tongue of His chosen servants. This guidance ensures that the creation of essences and bodies, which depend on foods for survival, is not foolish but enters into the realm of wisdom.

Correction: The author argues that creating only for annihilation is rationally ugly and outside wisdom; thus, a praiseworthy consequence (requiring divine guidance) is necessary.

B) They would perish quickly with no purpose, which is foolish.

D) They would not be created at all.

Key Takeaway
The second proof demonstrates that without divine guidance, creation would be foolish annihilation; thus, revelation is necessary to confer wisdom.

Creation Cannot Be for Annihilation Alone
Al-Nasafi establishes the principle that creation must have a wise purpose, necessitating divine guidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why creating the world solely for annihilation would be irrational, and why divine guidance is necessary to give creation meaning.

Core Idea
Creation for mere annihilation is foolish—only divine law gives it wisdom.

Al-Nasafi begins his third proof by establishing a foundational principle: any act of creation must have a worthy purpose. If the world were created only to perish without a positive outcome, that would be senseless. Therefore, there must be divine guidance to align creation with wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening premise
Read the Arabic text and translation. Notice how al-Nasafi describes the fragility of survival and the futility of creation for annihilation alone.
The phrase 'بدون حصول معنى لإيجادهم سوى الفناء' is key.
2
Identify the rational judgment
Recognize that al-Nasafi declares this scenario as 'مستقبح في العقول خارج عن الحكمة'—ugly in intellects and outside wisdom.
3
Understand the necessity of revelation
The conclusion: a statement (بيان) from the Creator is needed to elevate creation from foolishness to wisdom.
This sets up the need for prophets and divine law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقائها تلفت بأوهى مدة وأسرع زمان من غير حصول معنى لإيجادهم سوى الفناء، وخلق الخلق للفناء خاصة من غير عاقبة حميدة تتعلق به مستقبح في العقول خارج عن الحكمة فلا بد من البيان الوارد من منشئ الأشياء على طبائعها المختلفة، العالم بجواهرها وما يتعلق بها من الحكمة على لسان ما شاء من عباده، ليخرج تخليق الجواهر التي هي من أسباب البقاء وأحداث الأبدان المحتاجة في دوامها وبقائها إلى الأغذية المجعولة أسبابًا لذلك عن السفه ويدخل في حيز ما هو حكمة.

والثالث: أن بعد وقوفهم على ما يتعلق به بقاء أبدانهم، ولا شك أن كلا جبلوا على حب البقاء وطلب ما يحصل لهم به الدوام ، فلو لم يشرع لهم الحكيم شرعًا يأمرون بالتمسك به والانتهاء إلى حدوده مشتملاً على أسباب تبنى عليها الأحكام ويعرف بها اختصاص كل من اختص بشيء منها بما هو حكمه. وينقطع طمع من لاحظ له من تلك الأسباب عن الفوز بتلك الأحكام لتسارع كل إلى ما عرف به بقاءه ولتناول ما يرجو فيه دوامه، فيقع حينئذ بينهم أقبح تجاذب وأقطع تغالب، ثم يفضي ذلك إلى التقاتل، وذلك مما تؤول عاقبته إلى التفاني وانقطاع النسل وارتفاع الجنس وانعدام عاقبة لإيجاد الممتحنين سوى الفناء خاصة وذلك سفه.

وكذا لا شك أن في أجزاء العالم ما كانت الطبائع إليه مائلة والرغبات فيه ممتدة والنفوس إلى الاستيلاء عليه والاختصاص بالاستمتاع به متسارعة، والقلوب بنبله والظفر به والوصول إلى الارتفاق به منشرحة مرتاحة من نحو الجواري الحسان والغلمان الموصوفين بالجمال والدواب الفارهة، والدور الواسعة، والبساتين النزهة والأمتعة الفاخرة. فلولا الشيء الموجب اختصاص من اختص بسبب الملك لها لامتدت الأيدي الخاطفة الخاطئة والأطماع الفاسدة إلى كل من ذلك ولوقعت بينهم المنازعة المولدة للعداوة والبغضاء المورثة للضغائن والأحقاد، وكل ذلك مما يحمل على القتال وهو يؤدي إلى ما بيننا من انقطاع النسل وارتفاع الجنس المقصود بتخليق العالم، وذلك يوجب أن خلق الخلق لم يكن إلا للفناء خاصة وهو سفه جل ربنا عن ذلك وتعالى.

فإذا لا بد من شرع يبين اختصاص كل من البشر بما له من أصناف النعم بسبب يمتاز به عن غيره، ويحظر على من سواه ممن لا حظ له من سبب لتلك الأشياء منازعة أربابها المختصين بها لاختصاصهم بأسباب توجب لهم الملك فيها ليندفع الجدال ويرتفع الخصام، ويبقى العالم على ما له من الترتيب والنظام. فمن أنكر الشرع وأبطل الأمر والنهي فقد سعى في إثارة العبث والفساد في العالم، وإثبات أسباب التقاتل والتفاني، ونسب صانع العالم إلى السفه والجهل تعالى الله عما يقول الظالمون علوا كبيرا.

وبعد، فإنه لا عاقل في الشاهد يرضى من نفسه الانهماك في الشهوات وإعطاء النفس الأمارة بالسوء جميع ما تتمنى من الفواحش وتهوى من القبائح والاشتغال بالعبث والفساد، وظلم من سواه من العباد وإهمال العقل الذي هو من واهب الله الجزيلة ومنائحة الجليلة عن التفكر في حقائق الأشياء، واكتساب العلوم التي بإحرازها واقتنائها تشرف النفوس وتعظم الأخطار ويجل في أعين الخلق،
Its survival perishes in the weakest time and the quickest period without obtaining any meaning for their creation except annihilation, and creating creation for annihilation alone without a praiseworthy consequence attached to it is considered ugly in intellects and outside wisdom, so there must be a statement coming from the Originator of things upon their different natures, the Knower of their substances and what pertains to them of wisdom upon the tongue of whomever He wills of His servants, to remove the creation of substances that are causes of survival and the generation of bodies that need in their continuity and survival the foods made causes for that from foolishness and enter it into the realm of wisdom.

And the third: that after their knowing what pertains to the survival of their bodies, and there is no doubt that each is naturally disposed to love survival and seek what brings them continuity, so if the Wise One did not prescribe for them a law by which they are commanded to adhere to it and stop at its limits, including causes upon which judgments are built and by which is known the specialization of each who is specialized in something thereof according to its judgment, and the hope of one who has no share of those causes for attaining those judgments is cut off, so that each hastens to what he knows as his survival and takes what he hopes for his continuity, then there occurs among them the ugliest pulling and the most severe overcoming, then that leads to fighting, and that is something whose consequence leads to mutual annihilation, cessation of offspring, extinction of the species, and lack of consequence for the creation of the tested ones except annihilation alone, and that is foolishness.

And likewise there is no doubt that among the parts of the world are things toward which natures are inclined, desires are extended, souls are hastening to dominate and specialize in enjoyment, hearts are cheerful and at ease with their nobility, attainment, and benefit, such as beautiful slave girls, handsome boys, swift riding animals, spacious houses, pleasant gardens, and luxurious goods. Were it not for the thing that necessitates specialization of one who specializes due to a cause of ownership over them, then snatching hands and corrupt desires would extend to all of that, and there would occur among them conflict that generates enmity and hatred that bequeaths grudges and rancor, and all of that leads to fighting, and that leads to what we mentioned of cessation of offspring and extinction of the species intended by the creation of the world, and that necessitates that the creation of creatures was only for annihilation alone, and that is foolishness—glory be to our Lord above that and exalted.

So inevitably there must be a law that clarifies the specialization of every human being to what he has of kinds of blessings due to a cause by which he is distinguished from others, and prohibits others who have no share of a cause for those things from disputing with their owners who are specialized in them due to their specialization by causes that necessitate ownership for them, so that argument is repelled, dispute ceases, and the world remains upon its order and system. Whoever denies the law and nullifies command and prohibition has endeavored to stir up frivolity and corruption in the world, and to establish causes of fighting and mutual annihilation, and has attributed to the Maker of the world foolishness and ignorance—exalted is Allah far above what the wrongdoers say, a great exaltation.

Moreover, no rational person in the witnessed world would be pleased with himself by indulging in desires, giving the soul that commands evil all its cravings of obscenities and its whims of abominations, occupying himself with frivolity and corruption, oppressing other servants, and neglecting the intellect, which is from God's great gift and noble beneficence, from reflecting on the realities of things and acquiring sciences by whose acquisition and possession souls become noble, ranks become great, and one becomes esteemed in the eyes of creation.
Source pages p. 679

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof (burhan 'aqli) for the necessity of divine law (shar'). The author, al-Nasafi, presents the third argument in a series. The argument begins by noting that if creation were only for annihilation without a positive outcome, it would be foolish (safah) and contrary to wisdom (hikma). Therefore, divine guidance through a prophet is necessary to give meaning to creation. The author then launches into the third proof: humans naturally love survival and seek means to preserve themselves. If God did not prescribe a law defining rights and obligations, people would scramble selfishly for resources, leading to conflict, fighting, mutual destruction, and ultimately extinction of the human race. This outcome would be absurd (safah) and unworthy of a wise Creator. Next, al-Nasafi extends the argument to material goods and property. People naturally desire beautiful possessions, and without a system of ownership (milk) based on legitimate causes, there would be chaos, theft, and conflict. Law is needed to assign ownership rights and prevent anarchy. The author then concludes that denying the necessity of law amounts to promoting corruption and attributing foolishness to God. Finally, al-Nasafi appeals to common sense: no rational person would allow himself to be driven by base desires and neglect the intellect, which is a divine gift for discerning truth and acquiring knowledge. Thus, the need for law is rationally undeniable.

Key Terms
سفه (safah)
حكمة (hikma)
فناء (fana')
بقاء (baqa')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that creation can have no purpose other than annihilation, so life is meaningless.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues that creation must have a wise purpose; otherwise, it would be foolish and unworthy of a Wise Creator.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, what would be the rational status of creating the world solely for annihilation?
A) It would be wise.
B) It would be neutral.
C) It would be ugly and outside wisdom.
D) It would be praiseworthy.

Key Takeaway
The rational necessity of divine law is grounded in the need for creation to have a wise purpose.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that your entire existence was for nothing but annihilation, how would that change the way you live today? What does the fact that you are seeking knowledge from this lesson imply about your purpose?

The passage declares that creation without a wise purpose is intellectually repugnant. Consider the last year of your life: are there areas where you have been living as if this life is all there is, ignoring the eternal consequence? What is one concrete step you can take this week to align your actions with a purpose that transcends the grave?
?
Al-Nasafi states that without divine guidance, creation falls into foolishness. In what area of your life—career, relationships, or spirituality—are you relying solely on your own intellect, neglecting the guidance of revelation? What would it cost you to submit that area to the prophetic message, and are you willing to pay that price?

Human Survival Instinct Necessitates Law
Al-Nasafi argues that without divine law, human survival instinct causes destructive conflict.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the natural human desire for survival leads to conflict without divine law, and why law is needed to prevent mutual annihilation.

Core Idea
Without divine law, survival instinct leads to conflict, chaos, and extinction.

Al-Nasafi presents the core of the third proof: humans are naturally inclined to love survival and seek means to preserve themselves. If God did not prescribe a law defining rights and boundaries, people would selfishly compete for resources, leading to inevitable conflict and eventual extinction. This outcome is foolish and unworthy of a Wise Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument from survival instinct
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Note that it begins with 'والثالث: أن بعد وقوفهم على ما يتعلق به بقاء أبدانهم'. Al-Nasafi asserts that everyone loves survival.
2
Trace the chain of consequences
Follow the logical chain: no law → people scramble for survival → competition → conflict → fighting → mutual annihilation → extinction.
Highlight the phrase 'يقع حينئذ بينهم أقبح تجاذب وأقطع تغالب'.
3
Identify the absurd outcome
Al-Nasafi declares that such an outcome is 'سفه' (foolishness). This shows that the Wise Creator must prevent it by sending law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقائها تلفت بأوهى مدة وأسرع زمان من غير حصول معنى لإيجادهم سوى الفناء، وخلق الخلق للفناء خاصة من غير عاقبة حميدة تتعلق به مستقبح في العقول خارج عن الحكمة فلا بد من البيان الوارد من منشئ الأشياء على طبائعها المختلفة، العالم بجواهرها وما يتعلق بها من الحكمة على لسان ما شاء من عباده، ليخرج تخليق الجواهر التي هي من أسباب البقاء وأحداث الأبدان المحتاجة في دوامها وبقائها إلى الأغذية المجعولة أسبابًا لذلك عن السفه ويدخل في حيز ما هو حكمة.

والثالث: أن بعد وقوفهم على ما يتعلق به بقاء أبدانهم، ولا شك أن كلا جبلوا على حب البقاء وطلب ما يحصل لهم به الدوام ، فلو لم يشرع لهم الحكيم شرعًا يأمرون بالتمسك به والانتهاء إلى حدوده مشتملاً على أسباب تبنى عليها الأحكام ويعرف بها اختصاص كل من اختص بشيء منها بما هو حكمه. وينقطع طمع من لاحظ له من تلك الأسباب عن الفوز بتلك الأحكام لتسارع كل إلى ما عرف به بقاءه ولتناول ما يرجو فيه دوامه، فيقع حينئذ بينهم أقبح تجاذب وأقطع تغالب، ثم يفضي ذلك إلى التقاتل، وذلك مما تؤول عاقبته إلى التفاني وانقطاع النسل وارتفاع الجنس وانعدام عاقبة لإيجاد الممتحنين سوى الفناء خاصة وذلك سفه.

وكذا لا شك أن في أجزاء العالم ما كانت الطبائع إليه مائلة والرغبات فيه ممتدة والنفوس إلى الاستيلاء عليه والاختصاص بالاستمتاع به متسارعة، والقلوب بنبله والظفر به والوصول إلى الارتفاق به منشرحة مرتاحة من نحو الجواري الحسان والغلمان الموصوفين بالجمال والدواب الفارهة، والدور الواسعة، والبساتين النزهة والأمتعة الفاخرة. فلولا الشيء الموجب اختصاص من اختص بسبب الملك لها لامتدت الأيدي الخاطفة الخاطئة والأطماع الفاسدة إلى كل من ذلك ولوقعت بينهم المنازعة المولدة للعداوة والبغضاء المورثة للضغائن والأحقاد، وكل ذلك مما يحمل على القتال وهو يؤدي إلى ما بيننا من انقطاع النسل وارتفاع الجنس المقصود بتخليق العالم، وذلك يوجب أن خلق الخلق لم يكن إلا للفناء خاصة وهو سفه جل ربنا عن ذلك وتعالى.

فإذا لا بد من شرع يبين اختصاص كل من البشر بما له من أصناف النعم بسبب يمتاز به عن غيره، ويحظر على من سواه ممن لا حظ له من سبب لتلك الأشياء منازعة أربابها المختصين بها لاختصاصهم بأسباب توجب لهم الملك فيها ليندفع الجدال ويرتفع الخصام، ويبقى العالم على ما له من الترتيب والنظام. فمن أنكر الشرع وأبطل الأمر والنهي فقد سعى في إثارة العبث والفساد في العالم، وإثبات أسباب التقاتل والتفاني، ونسب صانع العالم إلى السفه والجهل تعالى الله عما يقول الظالمون علوا كبيرا.

وبعد، فإنه لا عاقل في الشاهد يرضى من نفسه الانهماك في الشهوات وإعطاء النفس الأمارة بالسوء جميع ما تتمنى من الفواحش وتهوى من القبائح والاشتغال بالعبث والفساد، وظلم من سواه من العباد وإهمال العقل الذي هو من واهب الله الجزيلة ومنائحة الجليلة عن التفكر في حقائق الأشياء، واكتساب العلوم التي بإحرازها واقتنائها تشرف النفوس وتعظم الأخطار ويجل في أعين الخلق،
Its survival perishes in the weakest time and the quickest period without obtaining any meaning for their creation except annihilation, and creating creation for annihilation alone without a praiseworthy consequence attached to it is considered ugly in intellects and outside wisdom, so there must be a statement coming from the Originator of things upon their different natures, the Knower of their substances and what pertains to them of wisdom upon the tongue of whomever He wills of His servants, to remove the creation of substances that are causes of survival and the generation of bodies that need in their continuity and survival the foods made causes for that from foolishness and enter it into the realm of wisdom.

And the third: that after their knowing what pertains to the survival of their bodies, and there is no doubt that each is naturally disposed to love survival and seek what brings them continuity, so if the Wise One did not prescribe for them a law by which they are commanded to adhere to it and stop at its limits, including causes upon which judgments are built and by which is known the specialization of each who is specialized in something thereof according to its judgment, and the hope of one who has no share of those causes for attaining those judgments is cut off, so that each hastens to what he knows as his survival and takes what he hopes for his continuity, then there occurs among them the ugliest pulling and the most severe overcoming, then that leads to fighting, and that is something whose consequence leads to mutual annihilation, cessation of offspring, extinction of the species, and lack of consequence for the creation of the tested ones except annihilation alone, and that is foolishness.

And likewise there is no doubt that among the parts of the world are things toward which natures are inclined, desires are extended, souls are hastening to dominate and specialize in enjoyment, hearts are cheerful and at ease with their nobility, attainment, and benefit, such as beautiful slave girls, handsome boys, swift riding animals, spacious houses, pleasant gardens, and luxurious goods. Were it not for the thing that necessitates specialization of one who specializes due to a cause of ownership over them, then snatching hands and corrupt desires would extend to all of that, and there would occur among them conflict that generates enmity and hatred that bequeaths grudges and rancor, and all of that leads to fighting, and that leads to what we mentioned of cessation of offspring and extinction of the species intended by the creation of the world, and that necessitates that the creation of creatures was only for annihilation alone, and that is foolishness—glory be to our Lord above that and exalted.

So inevitably there must be a law that clarifies the specialization of every human being to what he has of kinds of blessings due to a cause by which he is distinguished from others, and prohibits others who have no share of a cause for those things from disputing with their owners who are specialized in them due to their specialization by causes that necessitate ownership for them, so that argument is repelled, dispute ceases, and the world remains upon its order and system. Whoever denies the law and nullifies command and prohibition has endeavored to stir up frivolity and corruption in the world, and to establish causes of fighting and mutual annihilation, and has attributed to the Maker of the world foolishness and ignorance—exalted is Allah far above what the wrongdoers say, a great exaltation.

Moreover, no rational person in the witnessed world would be pleased with himself by indulging in desires, giving the soul that commands evil all its cravings of obscenities and its whims of abominations, occupying himself with frivolity and corruption, oppressing other servants, and neglecting the intellect, which is from God's great gift and noble beneficence, from reflecting on the realities of things and acquiring sciences by whose acquisition and possession souls become noble, ranks become great, and one becomes esteemed in the eyes of creation.
Source pages p. 679

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof (burhan 'aqli) for the necessity of divine law (shar'). The author, al-Nasafi, presents the third argument in a series. The argument begins by noting that if creation were only for annihilation without a positive outcome, it would be foolish (safah) and contrary to wisdom (hikma). Therefore, divine guidance through a prophet is necessary to give meaning to creation. The author then launches into the third proof: humans naturally love survival and seek means to preserve themselves. If God did not prescribe a law defining rights and obligations, people would scramble selfishly for resources, leading to conflict, fighting, mutual destruction, and ultimately extinction of the human race. This outcome would be absurd (safah) and unworthy of a wise Creator. Next, al-Nasafi extends the argument to material goods and property. People naturally desire beautiful possessions, and without a system of ownership (milk) based on legitimate causes, there would be chaos, theft, and conflict. Law is needed to assign ownership rights and prevent anarchy. The author then concludes that denying the necessity of law amounts to promoting corruption and attributing foolishness to God. Finally, al-Nasafi appeals to common sense: no rational person would allow himself to be driven by base desires and neglect the intellect, which is a divine gift for discerning truth and acquiring knowledge. Thus, the need for law is rationally undeniable.

Key Terms
شرع (shar')
بقاء (baqa')
فناء (fana')
تقاتل (taqatul)
سفه (safah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that humans can naturally come to peaceful agreements without divine law.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues that without an authoritative divine law, human greed and survival instinct inevitably lead to conflict and destruction.

Checkpoint
What does al-Nasafi say would be the ultimate consequence of not having divine law?
A) People would live in harmony.
B) Some would become wealthy, others poor but stable.
C) Mutual annihilation and extinction of the species.
D) People would invent their own laws.

Key Takeaway
Divine law is rationally necessary to prevent human nature from descending into mutual destruction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel that survival instinct pushing you to compete with others for status, wealth, or attention, do you immediately submit to Allah's limits, or do you let the ‘ugliest pulling’ take over? What would it look like to stop at His boundaries in that very moment?
?
Think of a time when you disregarded divine law to gain something you thought you needed for your ‘survival’. What was the result in your heart and relationships? Are you willing to repent and trust that His law is what truly preserves you, not your own grasping?
?
Al-Nasafi argues that without divine law, mutual annihilation is inevitable. In what areas of your life are you still living as if you are the ultimate judge of what you need, ignoring the Sharī‘ah? What is one concrete step you will take today to bind yourself to His limits, even if it feels like a loss?

Property Rights and the Necessity of Law
Al-Nasafi argues that desire for property necessitates divine law to define ownership and prevent anarchy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the natural desire for goods and property requires a divine law to establish ownership rights and prevent chaos.

Core Idea
Desire for possessions leads to conflict; law establishes ownership and preserves order.

Al-Nasafi extends his argument from survival to material possessions. People naturally desire beautiful items, land, and property. Without a system of ownership based on legitimate causes (أسباب), society would descend into theft and conflict. Therefore, a divine law is needed to clarify ownership and prohibit encroachment. He concludes that denying law promotes corruption and attributes foolishness to God.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument about possessions
Read the Arabic passage. Al-Nasafi lists examples of desirable things: slave girls, horses, houses, gardens, etc.
Note the contrast between lawful enjoyment and chaotic greed.
2
Understand the role of ownership causes
The law provides 'أسباب' (causes) that justify ownership, preventing conflict. Without these, everyone would grab what they desire.
3
Examine the conclusion
Al-Nasafi concludes that denying the law leads to corruption and attributing foolishness to God. He also appeals to reason: a rational person would not neglect intellect.
The final paragraph emphasizes the gift of intellect.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, what would happen if there were no divine law defining ownership?
A) People would voluntarily share everything.
B) Strong leaders would impose order.
C) Snatching hands and corrupt desires would lead to conflict and extinction.
D) People would peacefully trade.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see conflicts over property in the world—from your own disputes to global injustice—do you act as if divine law is irrelevant? If you truly believed that Allah's law alone can define just ownership, what would you change about how you handle your possessions or deal with others' claims? Give one concrete step.
?
Al-Nasafi says that denying the law attributes foolishness to God. When you neglect or downplay the role of Shari'ah in ordering your finances or relationships, are you in effect calling God's wisdom insufficient? What does this passage compel you to reexamine in your own life?
?
The intellect is a gift for reflecting on 'realities of things.' When was the last time you used your intellect to deeply contemplate the necessity of divine law for social order, rather than just accepting it as tradition? What might you be missing by not doing so?

Why Divine Law Is Needed for Ownership
Nasafi argues that divine law is needed to prevent conflict and chaos.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi argues that divine law is necessary to regulate ownership and prevent social chaos.

Core Idea
Without divine law, human greed leads to conflict and destruction.

This passage from Nasafi's Tabṣirat al-Adilla presents a rational argument for the necessity of prophetic law. The author begins by describing the beautiful and valuable things people naturally desire. He then imagines what would happen if there were no principle determining who owns what — chaos and mutual destruction. This leads to the conclusion that a divine law is essential for social order.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the flow from describing blessings to the hypothetical scenario and its conclusion.
The argument is built on everyday observations of human desire and conflict.
2
Identify the listed blessings
Nasafi lists several desirable things: beautiful women, handsome boys, swift horses, spacious houses, pleasant gardens, and luxurious goods. Why do you think he starts here?
These are things people naturally covet, setting up the need for a rule.
3
Trace the hypothetical chain
Imagine there were no cause for ownership. What happens? Hands snatch, disputes arise, leading to enmity, then fighting, then cessation of progeny, then extinction. Note the logical progression.
This chain shows the absurdity of creation without a law.
4
Understand the necessity of divine law
Nasafi concludes that a law (shar') is needed to specify each person's entitlement by a distinguishing cause, and to prohibit others from disputing it. This restores order.
The law must be divine, as human convention alone lacks binding authority.
5
Reflect on the condemnation
The passage ends by condemning those who deny divine law, accusing them of promoting corruption and attributing foolishness to God. Consider why this is a strong rhetorical move.
This ties the argument to the attributes of God (wisdom, justice).

الحسان والغلمان الموصوفين بالجمال والدواب الفارهة، والدور الواسعة، والبساتين النزهة والأمتعة الفاخرة. فلولا الشيء الموجب اختصاص من اختص بسبب الملك لها لامتدت الأيدي الخاطفة الخاطئة والأطماع الفاسدة إلى كل من ذلك ولوقعت بينهم المنازعة المولدة للعداوة والبغضاء المورثة للضغائن والأحقاد، وكل ذلك مما يحمل على القتال وهو يؤدي إلى ما بيننا من انقطاع النسل وارتفاع الجنس المقصود بتخليق العالم، وذلك يوجب أن خلق الخلق لم يكن إلا للفناء خاصة وهو سفه جل ربنا عن ذلك وتعالى. التملك فإذا لا بد من شرع يبين اختصاص كل من البشر بما له من أصناف النعم بسبب يمتاز به عن غيره، ويحظر على من سواه ممن لا حظ له من سبب لتلك الأشياء منازعة أربابها المختصين بها لاختصاصهم بأسباب توجب لهم الملك فيها ليندفع الجدال ويرتفع الخصام، ويبقى العالم على ما له من الترتيب والنظام. فمن أنكر الشرع وأبطل الأمر والنهي فقد سعى في إثارة العبث والفساد في العالم، وإثبات أسباب التقاتل والتفاني، ونسب صانع العالم إلى السفه والجهل تعالى الله عما يقول الظالمون علوا كبيرا.
Beautiful women and handsome boys, swift horses, spacious houses, pleasant gardens, and luxurious goods. Were it not for something that necessitates the specific attribution of ownership to someone due to a cause, then snatching, erroneous hands and corrupt desires would extend to all of that, and disputes would occur between them, generating enmity and hatred, bequeathing rancor and grudges. All of that leads to fighting, which results in the cessation of progeny and the elimination of the species intended by the creation of the world. That would necessitate that the creation of creatures was only for annihilation alone, and that is foolishness — our Lord is exalted above that and transcendent. Ownership: Thus there must be a law (shar') that specifies the entitlement of each human to the various types of blessings he possesses by a distinguishing cause, and prohibits others who have no share of that cause from disputing with their entitled owners due to their entitlement by causes that necessitate ownership for them, so that argument ceases, strife is removed, and the world remains in its proper order and system. Whoever denies the law (shar') and nullifies command and prohibition has striven to stir up frivolity and corruption in the world, and to establish causes of fighting and mutual destruction, and has attributed foolishness and ignorance to the Maker of the world — exalted is Allah above what the wrongdoers say, a great exaltation.
Source pages p. 680

Commentary
This passage argues for the necessity of divine law (shar') to regulate ownership and prevent social chaos. It begins by listing desirable worldly possessions — beautiful people, horses, houses, gardens, goods — and then poses a hypothetical: without a principle that determines why one person owns something and another does not, everyone would grab everything, leading to conflict, destruction of progeny, and ultimately the annihilation of the human race. That would mean creation was pointless, which is absurd for God. Therefore, a law (shar') is needed to specify each person's entitlement by a distinguishing cause (sabab) and to forbid others from disputing it. The passage then condemns anyone who rejects such a law, saying they promote corruption and attribute foolishness to God. The argument proceeds entirely from reason and observed human behavior, not from revealed texts.

Key Terms
شرع (shar')
ملك (ownership)
اختصاص (entitlement)
سبب (cause)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human convention or social agreement alone can establish binding ownership rights.
Correction: Nasafi argues that only a divine law (shar') can provide the necessary binding authority to prevent conflict, because human agreements lack the ultimate sanction to curb greed and enforce order.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what would happen if there were no principle determining ownership?
A) People would share everything equally.
B) Everyone would grab everything, leading to conflict and destruction.
C) The state would regulate ownership.
D) People would voluntarily refrain from greed.

Key Takeaway
Divine law is necessary to regulate ownership because without it, human greed leads to social chaos and the destruction of humanity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know your own heart: have you ever justified taking something that wasn't yours because you desired it? How does this passage expose the truth that without Divine boundaries, your own desires are a path to destruction? What will you do today to honor the distinction between what is yours and what belongs to others as defined by Allah's law?
?
When you look at the chaos in the world over resources, how do you see the truth of this argument playing out? But more importantly, where in your own life do you subtly reject the divine law's authority over your possessions? Will you commit to examining one area where you treat your ownership as absolute and independent of Allah's command?
?
The author says that rejecting divine law is to 'attribute foolishness and ignorance to the Maker.' Have you ever thought your own sense of fairness was enough? Do you truly believe that without Allah's law, you would be wise and just? What does that pride say about your view of Allah's wisdom?
