Why Reason Needs Prophets for Moral Specifics
Nasafi argues that reason needs prophetic guidance for specific good and evil acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's rational argument that human reason, while capable of recognizing good and evil in general, requires prophetic guidance to identify specific good and evil actions, making prophethood rationally necessary.

Core Idea
Reason knows the map, but prophets point out the exact locations.

Nasafi presents a compelling argument for the necessity of prophets that is grounded in the nature of human reason itself. He observes that rational people naturally seek honor and avoid blame, yet they are also prone to desires and ignorance. This leads to a conclusion that prophets are needed to discipline the soul. However, Nasafi refines this with a more precise observation: reason can only perceive general categories of good and evil, not their specific instances. Therefore, divine messengers are required to specify which actions are good or evil, enabling reason to act accordingly.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the flow of the argument from the initial description of rational behavior to the specific reasoning about general vs. particular knowledge.
Pay attention to the transition phrase 'يحقق هذا' which signals a verification of the previous point.
2
Identify the first argument
In the first part, Nasafi argues that no rational person would be satisfied with indulging desires and ignorance. Instead, they seek honor and wisdom. But due to innate ignorance and desires, they need someone who knows outcomes to guide them. This establishes the need for prophets.
This is a more general, ethical argument.
3
Identify the specific argument about categories
Nasafi then clarifies that reason is naturally inclined toward good and averse to evil, but it only knows these in their general forms (جمل), not specific instances (أعيان). To act rightly, one must know which particular acts are good or evil. Since only Allah knows the true nature of each act, prophets are necessary to convey this knowledge.
This is the core rational argument for prophethood.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this argument is powerful: it does not rely on scriptural authority but on the inherent limitations of human reason. It shows that prophethood is not arbitrary but a rational necessity.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد، فإنه لا عاقل في الشاهد يرضى من نفسه الانهماك في الشهوات وإعطاء النفس الأمارة بالسوء جميع ما تتمنى من الفواحش وتهوى من القبائح والاشتغال بالعبث والفساد، وظلم من سواه من العباد وإهمال العقل الذي هو من واهب الله الجزيلة ومنائحة الجليلة عن التفكر في حقائق الأشياء، واكتساب العلوم التي بإحرازها واقتنائها تشرف النفوس وتعظم الأخطار ويجل في أعين الخلق، ويترأس على دهماء الناس، وتصرف الوجوه إليها بالتعظيم والإجلال وتوجب صدورهم عن آرائهم فيما يحزبهم من الأمور والاقتضاء بهم فيما يأتون به ويذرونه، أو يرضى بنقيصة الجهل مع التمكن من دفعها والنزول على الدون من الدرجات معها في الوسع من الترقي إلى أعلاها، بل كل ذلك من العقلاء في عقولهم الاجتهاد على الإقبال على ما هو يحمد عليه من الأفعال، ويورث له الحمد والثناء الجميل ولسان الصدق والإعراض عما يوجب له ضده هذه الأحوال مما جبل كل منهم على الجهل الذي يعطيه بما يرجو به نجاته ونصره فيما به يطمع نفسه. ولا شك أن ما طبع عليه عقله مع ما جبل عليه هو من الجهل يخرجانه إلى من يعلم عواقب الأمور حتى يروض نفسه ويحملها على ما يدعو إليه عقله وينزجر عما يزجره عنه عقله على إشاراته دون أن يهملها وما هي بجبلتها تهواه وتميل إليه، وذلك يوجب القول بالرسل عليهم السلام لا محالة. يحقق هذا أن العقل في طبعه الميل إلى المحاسن والنفرة عن القبائح، ثم هو يقف على جمل المحاسن والمساوئ دون أعيانها، وكلياتها دون إفرادها ثم بعد هذا نقرر الكلام من وجهين: أحدهما أن الشرف والحكمة من الوقوف على أعيان ذلك دون الجهل إذ بذلك يمتاز الحكيم الماهر عن الغبي الجاهل فلا بد من ورود البيان مما له العلم بحقيقة كل فرد من أفراد تلك الجمل أنه من جملة المحاسن أو من جملة القبائح ليحمل العقل بميلانه إلى المحاسن صاحبه على مباشرته وتنافره عن القبائح على الانتهاء
Moreover, no rational person in the witnessed world is pleased with himself indulging in desires, giving the soul that commands evil all that it desires of lewd acts and that it inclines to of abominations, occupying himself with frivolity and corruption, oppressing others among the servants, and neglecting the intellect, which is among the generous gifts of Allah and noble bestowals, from reflecting on the realities of things and acquiring sciences by whose attainment souls become honored, dangers become great, one becomes esteemed in the eyes of people, gains leadership over the masses, faces turn to him with veneration and respect, they defer to his opinions in matters that befall them, and they follow him in what they do and leave. Or (would a rational person) be content with the deficiency of ignorance while able to repel it, and descend to the lowest ranks while it is within his capacity to ascend to the highest? Rather, all of that is such that rational people strive, by their intellects, to turn toward praiseworthy actions that bring them praise, beautiful commendation, and a good reputation, and to turn away from what brings them the opposite of these states, due to the ignorance that each of them is innately disposed to, which gives him what he hopes for his salvation and victory in what he desires for himself. There is no doubt that what his intellect is naturally disposed to, along with what he is innately disposed to of ignorance, both drive him to someone who knows the outcomes of things, so that he may discipline himself and compel it toward what his intellect calls him and restrain it from what his intellect forbids, following its signals, without neglecting it and what it by its nature desires and inclines to. That necessitates asserting the messengers (peace be upon them) without exception. This is verified by the fact that the intellect is naturally inclined toward good things and averse to bad things, yet it only identifies the general categories of good and evil without their specific instances, and their universals without their particulars. Then after this we state the matter in two ways: One is that honor and wisdom consist in knowing the specific instances of those categories rather than ignorance, for by that the skilled wise man is distinguished from the stupid ignorant. So there must be a clarification from one who has knowledge of the true nature of each individual of those categories, whether it belongs to the category of good or to the category of evil, so that the intellect, by its inclination toward good, may urge its owner to perform it, and by its aversion from evil, may keep him from it.
Source pages p. 680

Commentary
This passage argues for the necessity of prophets (rusul). It begins by describing the rational person's natural pursuit of honor, praise, and leadership, and his aversion to ignorance and blame. Despite this, humans are also innately inclined to ignorance and desire, which leads them astray. Therefore, they need someone who knows the true outcomes of actions — a prophet — to discipline their souls and guide them. The argument is then refined: reason naturally loves good and hates evil, but it only knows these in general terms (jimal), not their specific instances (a'yan). Since wisdom lies in knowing specifics, a divine messenger who knows the true nature of each act is needed to clarify whether it is good or evil. Thus the intellect can then act accordingly. The passage thus establishes the necessity of prophethood on rational grounds.

Key Terms
عقل (intellect)
رسل (messengers)
محاسن (goods)
قبائح (evils)
جمل (generals)
أعيان (specifics)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that human reason is fully capable of distinguishing good from evil in every specific situation without divine guidance.
Correction: Nasafi argues that reason only knows good and evil in general categories; it cannot determine the moral status of every specific act without prophetic specification.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why does the intellect need prophets?
A) Because the intellect is completely ignorant of good and evil.
B) Because the intellect only knows general good and evil, not specific instances.
C) Because the intellect is weak and cannot discipline itself.
D) Because the intellect has no desire for good.

Key Takeaway
Prophets are rationally necessary because reason only knows good and evil in general terms, not in specific applications, and only divine revelation can provide that specification.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what area of your life do you most often rely on your own sense of right and wrong rather than seeking prophetic guidance? What is the cost of that reliance?
?
What specific moral decision are you currently facing where you need a clear revelation from God? Have you truly subordinated your intellect to the Quran and Sunnah on that matter, or are you rationalizing your own inclination?
?
If you believe that prophets are necessary for moral specifics, how does that translate into your daily habits of seeking knowledge? Are you actively looking for prophetic rulings in your everyday choices, or do you assume your general sense is enough?

The First Proof for the Necessity of Prophets: Reason Knows Generals, Not Particulars
The author presents the first proof for the necessity of prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first proof for the necessity of prophethood: that human reason can perceive good and evil only in general terms, and divine revelation is needed to identify their specific instances.

Core Idea
Reason knows categories; revelation specifies acts.

Imam al-Nasafi begins his rational arguments for prophethood by examining the scope of human reason. He argues that while reason can distinguish between good and evil in the abstract, it cannot determine which particular actions fall under each category. This limitation demonstrates the need for prophetic guidance to complete our moral knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the logical connectors.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the main claim
Look for the sentence that states that honor and wisdom consist in knowing the specific instances (أعيان) of good and evil.
3
Understand the necessity
The author concludes that a statement (بيان) from one who knows the reality of each individual is required. Ask yourself: why is that necessary?
Consider the purpose of creating rational beings with inclinations.
4
Reflect on the consequence
If there were no such statement, the creation of rational beings with inclinations would be futile (عاقبة). This is the core of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم بعد هذا نقرر الكلام من وجهين: أحدهما أن الشرف والحكمة من الوقوف على أعيان ذلك دون الجهل إذ بذلك يمتاز الحكيم الماهر عن الغبي الجاهل فلا بد من ورود البيان مما له العلم بحقيقة كل فرد من أفراد تلك الجمل أنه من جملة المحاسن أو من جملة القبائح ليحمل العقل بميلانه إلى المحاسن صاحبه على مباشرته وتنافره عن القبائح على الانتهاء عنه فكذا لولا ذلك لم يحصل لتخليق العقلاء مائلاً إلى المحاسن نافرا عن القبائح عاقبة.
Then after this we settle the discourse from two aspects: The first is that honor and wisdom consist in knowing the specific instances of that [good and evil] without ignorance, for by that the skilled wise person is distinguished from the ignorant fool. So there must come a statement from one who has knowledge of the true nature of every individual of those universals, whether it is from the category of good or from the category of evil, so that the intellect, by its inclination towards goods, may lead its possessor to perform them, and by its aversion from evils, [lead him] to desist from them. For if that were not the case, the creation of rational beings as inclined towards goods and averse from evils would be fruitless.
Source pages p. 681

Commentary
This is a proof for the necessity of prophets. The author argues that reason alone can only know good and evil in general, not in their particular instances. Therefore, to achieve the purpose for which reason was created, divine revelation is needed to specify which acts are good and which are evil.

Key Terms
العقل
الحسن
القبيح
البيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That reason alone can fully determine moral obligations without revelation.
Correction: Reason knows only universal categories; it cannot identify which specific actions are good or evil without divine guidance.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, why is revelation necessary?
A) Reason is completely incapable of knowing good and evil.
B) Reason knows only general categories, not specific acts.
C) Reason is inherently corrupt.
D) Prophets are needed to enforce laws.

Key Takeaway
Prophets are necessary because human reason cannot specify the application of universal moral categories to particular actions.

Reason as Divine Command and the Need for Prophecy
Second proof: reason's inclination as divine command and prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second proof for the necessity of prophets: that reason's natural inclination to good and aversion from evil constitute a form of divine command, but require revelation to specify individual acts.

Core Idea
Reason is a built-in map, but only prophecy can label the destinations.

The author now presents a second argument for why prophets are necessary. This proof builds on the idea that our intellects are not self-sufficient: while reason inclines us toward good and away from evil, it cannot identify which specific acts are good or evil in detail. For that, we need divine guidance through prophets. This passage carefully explains the relationship between reason, divine command, and the role of revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the argument unfolds in a logical chain.
The author uses a conditional structure: 'if... then...'.
2
Identify the main claim
Find where the author states that intellect's inclination is the meaning of command and prohibition. Then trace how this leads to the need for revelation.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that a prophet is necessary to specify each act. Ask yourself why general inclination isn't enough.
This directly connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني: أن العاقل لو ترك ومجرد عقله مع أنه يميل إلى المحاسن وينفر عن القبائح ولا وقوف له على أفرادها بحقائقها من الحسن والقبح، وهو بميلانه إلى الحسن يدعو صاحبه إلى اكتسابه، وبنفاره ينهي صاحبه عن الإقدام عليه، وذلك هو معنى الأمر والنهي، إذ الأمر والنهي ليس إلا الدعاء إلى المباشرة والامتناع، والله تعالى هو الذي خلقه مائلاً إلى ما يميل إليه، نافرًا عما ينفر عنه، فيكون العقل دليل أمر الله ونهيه كالخطاب دليل أمره الذي هو صفته القائمة بذاته لما فيه من الدعاء إلى مباشرة فعل ودليل نهيه لما فيه من الدعاء إلى الامتناع عن مباشرة فعل العقل، ثم هو لما لم يقف على حقيقة كل فرد من أفراد العقل أنه من قبيل المحاسن أو من قبيل القبائح لم يعلم أنه مأمور به أو منهي عنه، فلو لم يرد الشرع ببيان محل كل فرد من أفراد الأفعال أنه من قبيل المحاسن أو من قبيل القبائح لبقى الأمر والنهي الحاصلان بالعقل على وجه لا يطاوع العمل بهما بمنزلة الأمر والنهي الواردين بالخطاب على سبيل الإجمال ولو لم يتصل البيان بالمجمل لما اهتدى المكلف إلى رفة ما أمر به ونهى عنه، ولا يتوصل إلى الائتمار والانتهاء، وذلك خارج عن حد الحكمة، فلابد حينئذ من ورود بيان سمعي على لسان من ارتضاه الصانع سفيراً بينه وبين عباده لتتحقق الحكمة في ذلك.
The second [aspect] is that if the rational person were left with his mere intellect, despite his inclination towards goods and aversion from evils, and he has no knowledge of their individual instances in their true reality of good and evil, while by his inclination towards good he calls his possessor to acquire it, and by his aversion he forbids his possessor from undertaking it—that is the meaning of command and prohibition, since command and prohibition are nothing but the call to performance and abstention—and God Most High is the One who created him inclined to what he inclines to, averse from what he is averse from; thus the intellect becomes an evidence of God's command and prohibition, like the articulated speech is evidence of His command, which is His attribute subsisting in His essence, because it contains a call to perform an act, and evidence of His prohibition because it contains a call to abstain from performing an act of the intellect. Then, since it does not have knowledge of the true nature of each individual act, whether it belongs to the category of goods or to the category of evils, it does not know whether it is commanded or prohibited. So if revelation did not come with an explication of the status of each individual act, whether it belongs to the category of goods or to the category of evils, the command and prohibition resulting from the intellect would remain in a manner not compliant with acting upon them, like the command and prohibition that come through articulated speech in a general way. And if the explication were not connected to the general, the responsible person would not be guided to the detail of what he is commanded and prohibited, nor would he attain compliance and abstention. That is outside the bounds of wisdom. Therefore, there must occur an auditory explication upon the tongue of one whom the Maker has chosen as an emissary between Him and His servants, so that wisdom may be realized in that.
Source pages p. 682

Commentary
This is the second proof for the necessity of prophets. The author argues that the intellect's natural inclination toward good and aversion from evil constitute a form of divine command and prohibition. Since God created these inclinations, the intellect becomes evidence of His command and prohibition, similar to how revealed speech evidences His attribute of command. However, the intellect cannot identify which specific acts are good or evil. Therefore, without revelation that specifies each act, the intellect's command and prohibition remain ineffective, like a general command that requires specification. Consequently, it is necessary for divine wisdom that a prophet be sent to provide this specification.

Key Terms
الأمر والنهي
العقل
الشرع
البيان السمعي
الحسن والقبح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Reason can determine the goodness or evil of every specific act without revelation.
Correction: The passage argues that reason only knows good and evil in general; it cannot identify each individual act's moral status. Revelation is needed to specify which acts are good or evil in detail.

Checkpoint
According to the second proof, why does the intellect need revelation to specify individual acts?
A) Because reason is inherently corrupt.
B) Because reason only knows good and evil in general, not in detail.
C) Because prophets are needed to create moral laws from scratch.
D) Because reason cannot produce any inclination towards good.

Key Takeaway
Reason provides a general orientation toward good and evil, but only prophetic revelation can specify which acts are actually commanded or prohibited.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have a natural pull toward what seems good and an aversion to what seems wrong. In what specific area of your life has your inclination led you astray, and how will you ensure you seek prophetic guidance before acting on it?
?
The author says that without revelation, the intellect's command remains 'not compliant with acting upon it'. Think of a moral dilemma you faced where your reason felt general but lacked detail. How will you commit to turning to the prophetic model for clarity next time?
?
Your intellect is a sign of God's command, yet it cannot specify each act. Are you content to rely on your reasoning alone, or will you humble yourself to seek the detailed guidance of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in your daily choices? What is one concrete step you can take today to bridge the gap?

The Need for Prophets: Even the Wisest Require Guidance
Nasafi proves the necessity of prophets through human deficiency and consultation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why even the most intelligent humans need prophets, based on inherent human deficiency and the universal practice of consultation.

Core Idea
Even the wisest need guidance; human deficiency proves the need for prophets.

This lesson examines a key proof for prophethood: the inherent limitation of human reason. Nasafi argues that even the most intelligent people require guidance, as shown by the universal practice of consultation. This leads to the necessity of divine messengers.

Guided Path
1

Prophets are the ultimate guides for matters beyond human reach.

Human Differences in Knowledge Necessitate Prophets
Nasafi argues from human epistemic diversity to the necessity of prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi uses human cognitive diversity as a proof for the necessity of prophets and why rejecting this implies claiming equality with God.

Core Idea
Because no human knows everything, prophets are necessary to convey what we cannot know by reason alone.

Nasafi presents a compelling argument from the observable fact that people differ in knowledge. If rational beings vary in their grasp of what is beneficial, then it is plausible that God possesses knowledge beyond human reach, which He communicates through prophets. Those who claim reason suffices inadvertently claim equality with God—a mark of extreme ignorance. This lesson unpacks the logic of this argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the premise about human differences
Read the first sentence and note the claim that rational people differ in perceiving their interests. This is the starting point of the argument.
2
Understand the inference to God's exclusive knowledge
Notice how Nasafi moves from human variation to the possibility that God has unique beneficial knowledge. Recognize that this is a logical step, not a leap.
The key phrase is 'فلا يدفع أن يكون عند الله تعالى شيء مما به صلاح عباده مما ليس عند خلقه'.
3
Recognize the refutation of intellectual self-sufficiency
The author then attacks the claim that reason alone is enough. Understand why claiming self-sufficiency implicitly claims equality with God.
This shows the severity of rejecting prophethood.

Source Text

And one has something of that which another does not have. This passage is a proof for the necessity of prophets based on human epistemic diversity. The author states the premise: rational people differ in their knowledge of interests. Since no single human possesses all beneficial knowledge, it is plausible that God possesses knowledge that humans lack, which He can transmit via messengers. The conclusion follows that anyone who claims reason is sufficient denies this inequality and implicitly claims equality with God, which is extreme ignorance.

The Necessity of Prophets: Even the Most Intelligent Need Guidance
The author argues from the need for guidance to the necessity of prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the universal need for guidance, even among the most intelligent, demonstrates the necessity of prophets.

Core Idea
Even the brightest minds need guidance—proving our need for prophets.

This passage presents a powerful argument for the necessity of prophets. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, points out that even the most intelligent and discerning people need guidance in their religious and worldly affairs. He grounds this in the universal human practice of seeking advice, showing that no one is self-sufficient. This sets the stage for understanding why prophets are essential.

The conclusion is that the rational cannot do without prophets for their interests in this world and the next.

Proof of Prophethood from Differences in Human Intellect
The author argues that variation in knowledge implies God's exclusive knowledge through prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the observable variation in human knowledge leads to the rational necessity of prophethood.

Core Idea
Our differences in knowledge prove God alone has complete knowledge to reveal.

This passage presents a proof for prophethood based on a simple observation: people differ in their understanding of what benefits them. If some know things others do not, then it is only logical that God possesses exclusive knowledge about human welfare that He conveys through messengers. The author then warns against the arrogance of claiming reason is sufficient without revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get its rhythm, then read the translation. Notice the key terms like 'تفاضل' (excell) and 'غنية بالعقل' (independence through reason).
2
Identify the key observation
The author starts with an undeniable fact: rational people vary in their knowledge of what benefits them in religion and worldly matters. One person knows something another does not.
This observation is the foundation of the argument.
3
Trace the logical inference
From the fact of variation, the author infers that it cannot be denied that Allah possesses something for the welfare of His servants that His creation does not have. This is then conveyed through messengers.
The inference is a straightforward 'if this, then cannot deny that'.
4
Reflect on the conclusion and warning
The author concludes by condemning anyone who claims human reason is sufficient, equating that claim to equating oneself with Allah in knowledge. This highlights the danger of arrogance.

The Necessity of Prophethood: An Initial Proof
Nasafi presents a logical proof for the necessity of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that revelation through prophets is necessary to know obligations and prohibitions, because without it, abandoning duties would be permissible, which contradicts divine wisdom.

Core Idea
Without revelation, abandoning obligations would be permissible, which is contrary to wisdom.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational proof for the necessity of prophethood as presented by Imam al-Nasafi. He builds an argument based on the need for knowledge of outcomes (عواقب الأمور) which only God can provide through chosen messengers. The argument shows that without such guidance, human action would be left in a state of uncertainty that undermines divine wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the key terms and the flow of the argument.
Focus on the conditional structure: 'if no revelation... then...'
2
Identify the logical steps
Break down the argument: premise (need for knowledge), hypothetical (no revelation), consequence (permissibility of abandoning obligations), contradiction (outside wisdom), conclusion (necessity of prophets).
3
Reflect on the implication
Why does Nasafi say this proves prophethood? Connect the argument to divine wisdom (الحكمة) and how revelation solves the problem.
Consider the final sentence about God never leaving humanity without proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحاجة إلى بيان من له الاطلاع على عواقب الأمور على لسان من ارتضاه من الرسل ليتمكن من أداء ما وجب منها والامتناع عما حرم، وهذه مقدمة لا خفاء بها على من له أدنى لبس. وقد يمكن أن يجمل عين هذا الكلام دليلاً للقول بوجوب الرسالة، إذ الأمر لما كان على ما بينا فلو لم يرد الوصول ببيان القسم الواسطة وقد يجب منه البعض لتعلق الحميد من العواقب به، ويحرم البعض التعلق الذميم من العواقب به لكان فيه إباحة ترك الواجب وإباحة مباشرة المحظور، وهو خارج عن الحكمة، فلابد من بيان ذلك ممن له العلم بذلك على لسان الرسول، ولهذا ما أخلى الله تعالى العالم منذ خلق الممتحنين عن الحجة السمعية. إما على ألسنة الرسل وإما على ألسنة خلفائهم، والله الموفق.
The need for a statement from the one who has knowledge of the outcomes of affairs upon the tongue of whom He has chosen from the messengers, so that he can perform what is obligatory from them and refrain from what is forbidden. And this is a premise that is not hidden from anyone who has the least intelligence. And it is possible that the very essence of this speech becomes a proof for the statement of the obligation of prophethood. For since the matter is as we have described, if the arrival (of revelation) with a statement of the intermediate category had not come — and some of it may be obligatory because a praiseworthy outcome is attached to it, and some is forbidden because a blameworthy outcome is attached to it — then there would be in that a permission to abandon the obligatory and a permission to commit the prohibited. And that is outside of wisdom. Therefore, a statement of that is necessary from the one who has knowledge of it upon the tongue of the messenger. And for this, Allah the Exalted has not emptied the world since He created the tested ones from the auditory proof, either upon the tongues of the messengers or upon the tongues of their successors. And Allah is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 686

Commentary
This passage is an initial proof for the necessity of prophethood (وجوب الرسالة). Nasafi begins by stating a clear premise: there is a need for someone who knows the outcomes of actions to clarify what is obligatory and what is forbidden, and this must come through the tongue of a messenger chosen by God. This premise is obvious to anyone with intelligence. He then argues that if we take the very idea of this premise and consider the situation where no revelation comes to explain which acts are obligatory (because they lead to praiseworthy outcomes) and which are forbidden (because they lead to blameworthy outcomes), then it would follow that it is permissible to abandon the obligatory and commit the prohibited — since without revelation, one would not know. But such permissibility is contrary to divine wisdom (الحكمة). Therefore, there must be a clarification from someone who knows, i.e., through the tongue of a messenger. Hence, throughout history, God has never left humanity without an auditory proof (الحجة السمعية), either through prophets or their successors.

Key Terms
وجوب الرسالة
الحكمة
الحجة السمعية
الممتحنين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human reason alone can determine all obligations and prohibitions without needing revelation.
Correction: Nasafi argues that without revelation, one cannot know which actions lead to praiseworthy or blameworthy outcomes, so reason alone is insufficient.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what would be the consequence if God did not send messengers to clarify obligations and prohibitions?
A) People would still be able to know them through reason alone.
B) There would be permission to abandon the obligatory and commit the prohibited, which is outside wisdom.
C) No consequence because human intellect is sufficient.
D) Only some people would be held accountable.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi's proof shows that revelation through prophets is necessary because without it, abandoning the obligatory would be permissible, which contradicts divine wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that without revelation, abandoning obligations would be permissible, then why do you sometimes ignore the revealed obligations in your daily life? What specific act have you neglected this week that the Prophet commanded, and what will you do today to rectify it?
?
The passage says Allah never leaves humanity without an auditory proof. Do you treat the Qur’an as that proof, or do you rely on your own reasoning to decide what is right and wrong? When you last faced a moral dilemma, did you first consult revelation or your own opinion? Commit now to check the source before acting next time.
?
Nasafi argues that without the prophet's clarification, we might treat the forbidden as permissible. Think of something you once thought was permissible but later learned was forbidden. How did you react? Are you currently holding onto any practice that you suspect might be prohibited but haven't investigated because it's comfortable? What will you do about it this week?

The Specific Need for Revelation: Three Categories of People
Nasafi explains the specific reason for revelation: the division of people into three intellectual categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why, according to Nasafi, the majority of people cannot rely solely on their intellect to know their obligations, and why revelation is necessary for them.

Core Idea
Revelation is needed because most people cannot reason their way to divine obligations.

Nasafi argues that while some rare individuals might grasp theological truths through reason alone, the vast majority of people fall into categories that cannot. He divides people into three groups based on their intellectual capacity and preoccupations. This lesson explores that division and explains why the second and third groups require divine guidance.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Nasafi is explaining why revelation is needed for obligatory matters. He gives two reasons; this lesson covers the first reason. First, read the passage and the translation to get the overall argument.
2
Identify the three categories
The passage describes three types of people: those with sharp intellects devoted to divine matters, those with sound intellects preoccupied with worldly affairs, and those with dull intellects dominated by base instincts. Find how each is described.
3
Analyze the sufficiency of each category
Nasafi claims the first category might be independent of revelation, but the second and third are not. Ask yourself: why can't the second and third groups rely on their intellects? The passage gives reasons.
The second group's intellect is limited to the immediate; the third group's intellect is too weak.
4
Reflect on the majority
Nasafi emphasizes that the first category is extremely rare. The lesson concludes that consideration is for the large multitude. Think about the implications for the necessity of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجه الحاجة إلى بيان الواجب والممتنع] على أن الحاجة ماسة في قسمي الواجب والممتنع اللذين في العقول إمكان الوقوف عليهما في الجملة، إلى البيان الوارد عن الله تعالى لمعنيين: أحدهما يختص ببعض العقلاء. والآخر يشمل الجميع. فأما المعنى الخاص فهو ما مر في أول الكتاب في مسألة إيمان المقلد من انقسام الناس إلى أقسام ثلاثة. أحدهما الموصوفون بحدة الخواطر والأذهان ووفور العقل والألباب، المتفرغون للتأمل والتفكر في المباحث النظرية والمعالم الإلهية، المعرضون عن الذات البهيمية والمطالب الجسمانية. والثاني: الموسومون برجاحة العقول وقوة الخواطر المشتغلون بالمصالح الدنيوية والمكاسب التي بها تقوم أسباب المعيشة للخلق المعرضون عن تعاطي النظر والاستدلال والتأمل في الدلائل العقلية. والثالث : المجبولون على بلادة الأفهام وغلظ الخواطر الذين استولت عليهم الطبيعة البهيمية والنفس السبعية. ثم من المعلوم أن القسم الأول إن كان لهم بعقولهم الوافرة المتفرغة للبحث عن حقائق الأمور والمعالم النظرية مندوحة عن الرسل وغنية عن اتصال المواد الوحيية بهم فيما يحتاجون إليه في مصالح داريهم، فلا غنية بالقسمين الآخرين عن ذلك، لقصر الفريق الثاني عقولهم وأذهانهم على اكتساب العاجلة وصرفهم جل همهم وكدحهم على استجلاب اللذات الحاضرة، وتعذر وقوف الفريق الثالث بما لهم من العقول الناقصة والأفهام البليدة على ما يجب عليهم من حقوق خالقهم وشكر ما أثنائه يتقلبون في أحوالهم من أنواع النعم وصنوف اللذات التي درت في جميع عليهم من صانعهم، بل انسداد طريق ذلك عليهم لو تركوا مجرد عقولهم فلابد لهم من بيان ذلك ليتوصلوا إلى شكر خالقهم، وما استحق عليهم من العبادة. فكان إرسال الله الرسول إليهم إثباتًا لطريق معرفته، والوقوف على ما افترض عليهم من حقوقه، كالمعقول في حق الفريق الأول. ولا شك أن القسم الأول بالإضافة إلى القسمين الآخرين في حد القلة والندارة بل في حد الشذوذ والندرة، وما هذا سبيله لا عبرة به ولا اكتراث له بل العبرة للجم الغفير والخلق الكثير والله الموفق. وأما المعنى الشامل لجميع طبقات العقلاء وهو أن العقل شيء مخلوق، لابد من لحوق الآفات به وحلول الفترة والكلال به عند استيلاء الضجر والملال على
[The aspect of the need for a statement of the obligatory and the impossible] As for the need being urgent in the two categories of the obligatory and the impossible which in the intellects there is possibility of grasping them in general, to the statement coming from Allah the Exalted for two meanings: one of them is specific to some rational beings, and the other includes all. As for the specific meaning, it is what passed at the beginning of the book in the issue of the faith of the imitator: the division of people into three categories. One of them: those described with sharpness of thoughts and minds, abundance of intellect and understanding, devoted to contemplation and reflection in theoretical investigations and divine matters, turning away from bestial desires and bodily demands. The second: those described with soundness of intellects and strength of thoughts, occupied with worldly interests and gains by which the means of livelihood for creation are established, turning away from engaging in investigation and inference and reflection in intellectual proofs. The third: those disposed with dullness of understanding and coarseness of thoughts, over whom the bestial nature and the predatory soul have prevailed. Then it is known that if the first category, with their abundant intellects devoted to research into the truths of things and theoretical matters, have independence from messengers and are free from need for the attachment of revelatory materials to them in what they need for the interests of their two abodes, then the other two categories have no independence from that, because the second group's intellects and minds are limited to acquiring the immediate and they spend the majority of their effort and toil on seeking present pleasures, and because it is difficult for the third group, with their deficient intellects and dull understandings, to grasp what is obligatory upon them of the rights of their Creator and gratitude for what His blessings they turn over in their states from the varieties of favors and kinds of pleasures that have continually flowed upon them from their Maker. Rather, the path to that is blocked for them if they are left to their mere intellects. So they must have a statement of that in order to reach gratitude to their Creator and what is incumbent upon them of worship. So sending the messenger to them was an establishment of the path of knowledge of Him and pausing upon what He has imposed upon them of His rights, like what is intelligible concerning the first category. And there is no doubt that the first category, in relation to the other two categories, is at the limit of scarcity and rarity, rather at the limit of oddity and rareness. And what is like this is not regarded nor paid attention to; rather, consideration is for the large multitude and the many creation. And Allah is the Giver of success. And as for the meaning inclusive of all classes of rational beings: that the intellect is something created, inevitably affected by defects, and the onset of languor and fatigue enters it when boredom and weariness overcome.
Source pages p. 686

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the need for divine revelation (البيان) concerning the obligatory (الواجب) and the impossible (الممتنع), even though reason can grasp them in general. Nasafi presents two meanings (معنيين) for this need: one specific to some rational beings and one general to all. The specific meaning is based on the division of people into three categories, which he previously mentioned in the discussion of the faith of the imitator. The first category comprises those with keen minds, abundant intellect, and leisure for theoretical and divine investigations; they may be independent of messengers. The second category consists of those with sound intellects but who are preoccupied with worldly affairs and do not engage in theoretical reasoning. The third category are those with dull intellects and coarse natures, dominated by animalistic instincts. Nasafi then argues that while the first category might be self-sufficient, the other two are in dire need of revelation: the second because their intellects are focused on immediate gains, and the third because their intellects are too weak to grasp their obligations. He emphasizes that the first category is extremely rare and negligible compared to the vast majority (الجم الغفير). The general meaning applicable to all rational beings is that the intellect itself is a created thing, subject to defects, fatigue, and boredom, and thus cannot be relied upon exclusively without divine guidance.

Key Terms
الواجب
الممتنع
البيان
المعنى الخاص
المقلد
الجم الغفير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that because some people can reason out obligations, revelation is not needed for anyone.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that the majority cannot reason properly; the elite who can are extremely rare, so revelation is necessary for the masses.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why are the second and third categories of people in need of revelation?
A) Because their intellects are completely absent.
B) Because the second category's intellects are limited to worldly gains and the third category's intellects are too dull.
C) Because they refuse to use their intellects.
D) Because revelation is needed even for the first category.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi argues that the specific reason revelation is needed is that the majority of people (the second and third categories) cannot independently reason to know their obligations to God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the three categories do you most resemble based on your daily focus and intellectual habits? Are you among the elite devoted to contemplation, the worldly occupied with immediate gains, or the dull unaware of your obligations? What does your schedule reveal about your true priorities?
?
If you find yourself in the second category, how much of your effort is spent on worldly interests versus learning your duties to Allah? What is one concrete change you can make this week to shift your focus towards the afterlife?
?
Do you ever rely solely on your intellect to determine what Allah expects of you, neglecting revelation? In what area of your life have you assumed you already know your obligations without consulting the Qur'an and Sunnah? Make a commitment today to seek divine guidance in that matter.

The General Need for Revelation: The Weakness of the Intellect
Nasafi presents the universal reason: the intellect is created and therefore weak.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's second, universal reason for revelation: that the intellect itself is a created thing subject to defects and fatigue.

Core Idea
Even the strongest intellect is a created thing that grows weak and needs revelation.

Beyond the specific need based on categories of people, Nasafi presents a universal reason applicable to all rational beings. He asserts that the intellect is a created entity that inherently suffers from defects, fatigue, and boredom. This fragility means that even for those capable of reasoning, reliance on intellect alone is insufficient. This lesson examines that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the short passage
The passage for this lesson is brief but dense. Read the Arabic and translation carefully.
It is the second meaning that Nasafi mentions.
2
Understand the claim
Nasafi states that the intellect is a created thing (مخلوق). What does that imply? Creation is subject to change and weakness.
3
Identify the defects
The passage mentions that the intellect is inevitably affected by defects (الآفات) and experiences fatigue (الفترة) and boredom (الملال). Why is this significant?
4
Connect to the need for revelation
Because the intellect is prone to error and weariness, it cannot be a perfect guide on its own. Thus, even the sharpest minds need divine revelation as a corrective and supplement.
This complements the specific reason.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi's general meaning, why is the intellect insufficient on its own?
A) Because it is not created.
B) Because it is created and therefore subject to defects, fatigue, and boredom.
C) Because it cannot grasp the obligatory at all.
D) Because it only works for the first category of people.

Nasafi's universal reason for revelation is that the intellect, being created, is inherently weak and prone to error, so divine guidance is needed for all.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent moment when you were certain about a religious matter based on your own reasoning, only to later realize you were mistaken. How does Nasafi's description of the intellect's weakness speak to that experience? Will you now doubt your own reasoning and turn more to revelation before forming opinions?
?
Your intellect is a gift from Allah, but it is also created and limited. In which area of your life—your beliefs, your judgments about others, or your spiritual decisions—are you most tempted to trust your intellect alone? What would change if you consciously submitted that area to divine guidance today?
?
When you feel bored or weary in your religious practice, your intellect may become slack. How has your mood or tiredness ever led you to doubt or neglect core teachings? What specific step will you take this week to reconnect with revelation when you feel spiritually fatigued?

Why the Majority Needs Prophets: A Classification of People
Classification of people and argument for necessity of prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's classification of people into three categories based on intellectual capacity and his argument that the majority requires prophetic guidance.

Core Idea
Prophets are necessary for most people because their intellects are either preoccupied or deficient.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi presents a key argument for the necessity of prophethood. He classifies people into three types: those with perfect intellects, those engrossed in worldly pursuits, and those with dull minds. While the first may not need prophets, the other two cannot fulfill their duties to God without revelation. The passage concludes that the first group is extremely rare, so the need for prophets is universal for all practical purposes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the author describes the second and third categories of people.
The first category is not described in detail here but is referenced later.
2
Identify the descriptions of the second and third categories
Find where the author describes the second category as those who turn away from reflection, and the third as those with dull intellects and bestial natures.
3
Understand the conditional argument
The author says: if the first category can do without prophets (due to their abundant intellects), then the other two categories cannot. Trace this logic.
Note the phrase 'فلا غنية بالقسمين الآخرين عن ذلك'.
4
Analyze each group's deficiency
The second group is limited by focusing on worldly gains; the third group has deficient intellects and cannot grasp divine duties on their own.
5
Reflect on the conclusion about rarity
The author states that the first group is extremely rare, even at the level of oddness. Therefore, the majority of humanity needs prophets.
This reinforces the universal necessity of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدنيوية والمكاسب التي بها تقوم أسباب المعيشة للخلق المعرضون عن تعاطي النظر والاستدلال والتأمل في الدلائل العقلية. والثالث : المجبولون على بلادة الأفهام وغلظ الخواطر الذين استولت عليهم الطبيعة البهيمية والنفس السبعية. ثم من المعلوم أن القسم الأول إن كان لهم بعقولهم الوافرة المتفرغة للبحث عن حقائق الأمور والمعالم النظرية مندوحة عن الرسل وغنية عن اتصال المواد الوحيية بهم فيما يحتاجون إليه في مصالح داريهم، فلا غنية بالقسمين الآخرين عن ذلك، لقصر الفريق الثاني عقولهم وأذهانهم على اكتساب العاجلة وصرفهم جل همهم وكدحهم على استجلاب اللذات الحاضرة، وتعذر وقوف الفريق الثالث بما لهم من العقول الناقصة والأفهام البليدة على ما يجب عليهم من حقوق خالقهم وشكر ما أثنائه يتقلبون في أحوالهم من أنواع النعم وصنوف اللذات التي درت في جميع عليهم من صانعهم، بل انسداد طريق ذلك عليهم لو تركوا مجرد عقولهم فلابد لهم من بيان ذلك ليتوصلوا إلى شكر خالقهم، وما استحق عليهم من العبادة. فكان إرسال الله الرسول إليهم إثباتًا لطريق معرفته، والوقوف على ما افترض عليهم من حقوقه، كالمعقول في حق الفريق الأول. ولا شك أن القسم الأول بالإضافة إلى القسمين الآخرين في حد القلة والندارة بل في حد الشذوذ والندرة، وما هذا سبيله لا عبرة به ولا اكتراث له بل العبرة للجم الغفير والخلق الكثير والله الموفق.
The worldly [pursuits] and acquisitions by which the means of livelihood are established for the creatures who turn away from engaging in reflection, inference, and contemplation of intellectual proofs. And the third: those created with dullness of understanding and coarseness of thoughts, over whom the bestial nature and the predatory soul have prevailed. Then it is known that the first category—if they have, by their abundant intellects devoted to investigating the realities of things and theoretical principles, an independence from messengers and a freedom from need for connection to revelatory materials for what they require in the interests of their two abodes—then the other two categories are not independent of that, due to the limitation of the second group's intellects and minds to acquiring the immediate [world] and their devotion of most of their concern and effort to obtaining present pleasures, and the impossibility for the third group, with their deficient intellects and dull understandings, of comprehending what is obligatory upon them of the rights of their Creator and gratitude for what He has—in which they are turning over in their states—of the kinds of blessings and varieties of pleasures that have flowed continually upon them from their Maker. Rather, the path to that is blocked for them if they were left to their mere intellects, so they must have an explanation of that to attain gratitude to their Creator and what He deserves of worship. So the sending of God's messenger to them was an establishment of the path to knowing Him and understanding what He has imposed upon them of His rights, similar to what is intellectually understood regarding the first group. There is no doubt that the first group, in comparison to the other two groups, is at the limit of scarcity and rarity, rather at the limit of oddness and rarity. What is in this state is not regarded nor heeded; rather, regard is for the great multitude and the many people. And God is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 687

Commentary
This passage is a classification and argument. The author describes two of three categories of people (the first was described previously). The second category consists of those preoccupied with worldly gains, turning away from intellectual reflection. The third are those with dull intellects and bestial natures. The argument then proceeds: if the first category—those with ample intellects devoted to seeking truth—can do without prophets and revelation, then the other two categories cannot, because the second group's minds are occupied with immediate pleasures, and the third group's deficient intellects prevent them from knowing their duties. Thus, they need prophetic guidance to achieve gratitude and worship. The author concludes that the first category is extremely rare, so the majority requires prophets; the minority is negligible.

Key Terms
القسم الثاني
القسم الثالث
الرسل
الوحي
النظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People with perfect intellects are common and can do without prophets.
Correction: The author explicitly states that the first category is extremely rare, even odd, so practically everyone needs prophets.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why do the second and third categories of people need prophets?
A) Because they lack intellect entirely.
B) Because their intellects are either preoccupied with worldly gains or too dull to grasp divine duties.
C) Because prophets are needed even for the first category.
D) Because revelation is always required for all acts of worship.

Key Takeaway
The majority of humanity cannot know God's rights through intellect alone because their minds are either occupied with worldly pursuits or too dull; thus, prophets are a universal necessity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you more like the second group—so busy with worldly gains and pleasures that you neglect reflection on God's signs? What is one immediate pleasure you can sacrifice this week to create space for that reflection?
?
Do you ever secretly feel that your intellect is sufficient to know God's rights without regularly consulting revelation? How does this lesson expose the arrogance of that assumption, and what step will you take to humble yourself before the revealed guidance?
?
If you consider yourself among the rare first group—those with strong intellects—who do you think is responsible for guiding the majority who need revelation? How will you use your understanding to serve those who struggle to see God's signs?

The Weakness of the Intellect and the Need for Revelation
The author argues for the necessity of revelation due to the created nature and weaknesses of the intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the intellect, though capable, is inherently weak and why divine revelation is essential as an aid to access true knowledge.

Core Idea
The intellect needs revelation because it is created and prone to weaknesses that only divine guidance can overcome.

The author of the Tabṣirat al-Adilla begins with a fundamental point: the intellect is created, and therefore subject to limitations. He lists various afflictions that hinder rational thought, from doubts and desires to physical pains. These obstacles make it impossible for the intellect to reach necessary truths on its own. Thus, revelation is not a luxury but a necessity. In this passage, you will see the rational argument for why revelation must complement the intellect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the overall argument. Notice how the author lists multiple weaknesses.
2
Identify the key weaknesses of the intellect
The author states that the intellect is created (مخلوق) and therefore subject to defects. List the specific obstacles he mentions: defects, languor, doubts, desires, worries, pains, etc.
3
Understand the role of revelation
After establishing the intellect's limitations, the author introduces revelation as the necessary assistant (معاون). Note how revelation helps not only the weak but also the capable by easing the burden.
4
Reflect on the practical implication
Consider why this argument is important: it shows that human reason is not sufficient for salvation; guidance from God is required. This is a foundational point in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العقل مخلوق لذا يلحقه الضعف: وأما المعنى الشامل لجميع طبقات العقلاء وهو أن العقل شيء مخلوق، لابد من لحوق الآفات به وحلول الفترة والكلال به عند استيلاء الضجر والملال على صاحبه، وربما تعارضه الشبهات، وتصده عن حقيقة النظر الأماني والشهوات، وتمنعه عن الإحاطة بكل دقيق من الأمور وجليل، اعتراء الهموم وأسباب شغل القلب على صاحبه، وترادف الآلام والأوجاع عليه، وتشغله عن الاستقصاء في البحث والتأمل مع ما في المطالب النظرية من الغموض والدقة فلابد من معاون له إياه ليصل باتصاله به إلى ما يجب الوصول إليه. وذلك هو الوحي السماوي، والله الموفق. على أن العقول لو كان في جبلتها إمكان الوصول إلى جميع مصالح الدارين إلا أن ذلك لن يكون إلا بآداب الفكر، ونصّ مطية الخاطر، والانكباب على النظر الدائم والبحث الكامل، ويلحقه بذلك مشقة عظيمة، وتلزمه مؤنة كثيرة. ثم إنه إذا نبه على ذلك بالسمع وأرشد إلى كيفية استخراج ما يرومه بعقله تنبه لذلك، وسهل عليه الأمر وخفت له المؤنة.
The intellect is created, hence weakness afflicts it. As for the comprehensive meaning applying to all strata of the rational: it is that the intellect is a created thing; it is inevitable that defects afflict it, that languor and fatigue overtake it when boredom and weariness overcome its possessor; sometimes doubts oppose it, and desires and passions turn it away from the reality of reflection; they prevent it from encompassing every fine and coarse matter; the onset of worries and causes of heart-occupation [afflict] its possessor, and the succession of pains and ailments upon him, and they occupy him from exhaustive investigation and contemplation, along with what is in theoretical demands of subtlety and precision. So he must have an assistant that aids him so that by connection with it he may reach what must be reached. That is divine revelation. And God is the giver of success. Moreover, even if it were in the innate disposition of intellects the possibility of reaching all interests of the two abodes, that would not be except through the disciplines of thought, the exertion of the mind, and devotion to constant reflection and complete investigation; and great hardship attaches to that, and much burden is required. Then, if he is alerted to that by [scriptural] hearing and guided to the method of extracting what he seeks by his intellect, he becomes alert to it, the matter becomes easy for him, and the burden becomes light for him.
Source pages p. 687

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the need for revelation based on the nature of the intellect. The author begins by stating that the intellect is created, therefore subject to weakness. He then lists various afflictions: defects, fatigue, doubts, desires, worries, pains, and the subtlety of theoretical subjects. Because of these, the intellect needs an assistant—divine revelation. The author further argues that even if intellects could theoretically reach all goals, doing so would require immense effort and hardship; revelation eases this task by providing guidance. Thus revelation is not just necessary for the incapable but also beneficial for all.

Key Terms
العقل
الوحي السماوي
الآفات
الشبهات
النظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The intellect is fully self-sufficient for all knowledge, including religious truths.
Correction: The passage demonstrates that the intellect is created and subject to numerous weaknesses, and even for the capable, the effort is immense; thus revelation is needed to assist and ease the path.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is revelation necessary despite the intellect's potential?
A) Because the intellect is always evil.
B) Because the intellect is created and subject to weaknesses and obstacles, and even when capable, the effort is great; revelation eases the path.
C) Because revelation is needed only for the ignorant.
D) Because the intellect cannot grasp any truth at all.

Key Takeaway
The intellect, being created, is inherently weak and prone to obstacles; divine revelation is the necessary assistant that enables it to reach the truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the weaknesses listed in the passage—such as boredom, doubts, desires, or worries—do you most often experience when trying to understand your faith honestly? What specific step will you take today to turn to revelation as your assistant in that area?
?
The author says revelation makes the burden light. What burden are you currently carrying in your search for truth that you have not yet placed before divine guidance? Will you open the scripture right now and ask for clarity?
?
If even the strongest intellect cannot reach all truth without hardship, where are you relying on your own reasoning instead of submitting to revelation in matters of creed or practice? What is one truth you have avoided accepting because your intellect struggles with it? How will you connect with revelation to overcome that struggle?

Revelation Guarantees Truth Over Intellect Alone
Contrast between prophets' followers and philosophers to show necessity of revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why revelation is necessary for attaining truth, as illustrated by the contrast between followers of prophets and philosophers.

Core Idea
Revelation guides the simple to truth; intellect alone can lead the brilliant astray.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi presents a striking historical observation: the followers of prophets, despite their lack of philosophical training, consistently adhere to the truth, while philosophers, with all their intellectual rigor, frequently fall into error. The author attributes this difference to the support of revelation. Let's examine this argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its English translation. Notice the contrast being drawn between two groups.
2
Identify the key contrast
The passage contrasts two groups: the followers of prophets and the philosophers. Note the characteristics of each group.
The followers are described as dull and occupied with livelihood, yet they cling to truth. Philosophers are intellectually sharp but fall into disbelief.
3
Understand the reason for the contrast
The passage ends by giving the reason: the first group is supported by 'the material of revelation' (مادة الوحي). This is the key point.
Revelation provides a source of truth that intellect alone cannot guarantee.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider what this says about the necessity of revelation for guidance. How does it challenge the idea that human reason is sufficient?
This connects to the broader theological claim that prophecy and revelation are essential.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا كان الغالب في اتباع الأنبياء عليهم السلام الاستمرار على الحق والتشبث به، وإن كان أكثرهم خالين عن صناعة النظر موصوفين بالبلادة، مشغولين باكتساب أسباب المعاش والغالب على الفلاسفة العدول عن الصواب والوقوع في الكفر والضلال، وإن كانوا موصوفين برجاحة العقول وقوة الألباب وصفاء القرائح، متفرغين سنين كثيرة وأعمارًا طويلة للبحث عن المعالم الإلهية والمعاني الدينية، معتزلين الخلق في مدارسهم، لتأيد الصنف الأول بمادة الوحي
For this reason, the prevailing characteristic in the followers of the prophets, peace be upon them, is persistence upon truth and clinging to it, even though most of them are devoid of the art of speculation, described as dullness, occupied with acquiring means of livelihood—while the prevailing characteristic of the philosophers is deviation from correctness and falling into unbelief and misguidance, even though they are described as having soundness of intellects, strength of minds, and purity of innate dispositions, having devoted many years and long lifetimes to the investigation of divine principles and religious meanings, isolating themselves from people in their schools—because the first group is supported by the material of revelation.
Source pages p. 688

Commentary
This passage presents a comparative observation as evidence for the necessity and efficacy of revelation. The author notes that the followers of prophets, despite often lacking speculative skills and being occupied with worldly work, consistently adhere to truth. In contrast, philosophers, despite their sharp intellects, long study, and dedication, frequently fall into error and disbelief. The reason given is that the prophets' followers are supported by revelation, which provides guidance that reason alone cannot guarantee.

Key Terms
الأنبياء
الفلاسفة
الوحي
الحق
الضلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might assume that intellectual sophistication and rigorous study guarantee arriving at truth, especially in theological matters.
Correction: The passage shows that despite their intellectual advantages, philosophers often fall into error, while the simple followers of prophets adhere to truth. The decisive factor is revelation, not intellect.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes the followers of prophets from philosophers in terms of their access to truth?
A) Followers of prophets are more intelligent.
B) Philosophers lack the material of revelation.
C) Followers of prophets study longer.
D) Philosophers are not sincere.

Key Takeaway
Revelation provides a sure guide to truth that even the most brilliant intellects cannot guarantee on their own.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you, like the philosophers, relying on your own intellect and knowledge to find truth, while neglecting the revealed guidance that even the simple can follow? What specific step will you take today to ensure revelation guides your mind?
?
The followers of prophets are described as dull and busy with livelihood, yet they cling to truth. Do you consider yourself too busy or too intelligent to need constant recourse to revelation? How will you change that?
?
The philosophers devoted years to divine studies yet fell into misguidance. Are you confident that your own study of religion is grounded in revelation rather than your own reasoning? What evidence in your life shows that you submit to revelation over your intellect?
